Mr. Zou specially took a train from Beijing to Shanghai around 7:00 AM yesterday to seek instructions.

Joint Handling of Domestic Rice Transportation and Discounted Exchange by China, Jiaotong, and Other Banks; Total Amount Tentatively Set at 10 Million Yuan at 7% Interest; Starting with Hunan Rice to Guangdong, Gradually Promoting to Other Areas; Specific Measures to Be Decided Next Week and Undertaken 95

According to the Xin Xin News Agency, China, Jiaotong, and ten other banks will jointly handle the discounted exchange loan for the transportation and sale of domestic rice in order to assist the government in developing agriculture and regulating food supply. It has been decided to start with Hunan rice to Guangdong, with the total loan amount tentatively set at 10 million yuan. Another meeting will be held next week to determine specific measures, and implementation will begin immediately. Details are as follows:

Assisting the Government in Regulating Food Supply

China, Jiaotong, and other banks believe that this year's harvest is abundant in various places, and the government has specifically negotiated with state-owned railways and China Merchants Group and other transportation agencies to reduce transportation prices to facilitate farmers and merchants. In order to assist the government in regulating food supply, it has been proposed to jointly organize various banks to handle the discounted exchange loan for rice transportation and sales. The so-called discounted exchange for transportation and sales is, for example, if a place A has 10,000 yuan worth of rice to be transported to a merchant in place B for sale, the loan can only be obtained after the rice arrives at the destination. If discounted exchange is handled, the seller in place A only needs to transport the goods to place B, and then hand over the bill of lading, insurance policy, invoice, etc. to the bank that handles the discounted exchange to obtain the payment first. After the goods arrive in place B, the buyer in place B will return the payment to the bank and receive the bill of lading to pick up the goods. The bank that handles the transaction will take a commission, which is the interest on the loan.

Three Major Principles for Handling Discounted Exchange

Since the China and Jiaotong Banks initiated the organization, they have invited representatives from various banks to meet at the Bank of China. Initially, the plan was to only handle the discounted exchange loan for Hunan rice to Guangdong. However, according to the opinions of the majority, it was considered that the rice production has increased sharply this year, and if only Hunan rice is handled, the scope seems too narrow. It was decided to expand the scope, and all domestic rice will be accepted for discounted exchange, but only those that meet the following principles and have been negotiated in advance: (1) Rice produced in the Republic of China, (2) Rice that has been formally inspected and qualified by the Ministry of Industry, (3) Rice merchants and customers who have credit in normal times. All rice that meets the above principles will be accepted for processing, and the specific measures for Hunan rice to Guangdong have been negotiated and agreed upon by the two provincial governments. Therefore, it has been decided to start with Hunan rice and gradually promote it to other provinces.

Meeting Next Week to Discuss Implementation Measures

Reporters learned from participating banks yesterday that the organization was initiated by the China and Jiaotong Banks. As of yesterday, the participants included China, Jiaotong, Shanghai, Jin Cheng, Mainland, Yantian, Zhongnan, Guohua, China National Products, and Postal Savings Bureau. The Four Bank Savings Society and the Farmers Bank of China did not participate. At the meeting held at the Bank of China the other day, in addition to deciding on the processing principles, the total loan amount was also tentatively set at 10 million yuan, which will be increased or decreased at any time depending on the needs. The minimum interest rate is 7%, and the loans will be automatically undertaken by each bank. In order to reduce costs, it is not planned to establish a formal banking group, and the China and Jiaotong Banks are publicly nominated as representatives to be responsible for hosting everything. It is planned to convene another meeting of representatives from various banks next week to determine the specific implementation measures, and then implementation will begin immediately. There is no need to sign a contract with any rice merchants or groups.

China Merchants Group: Strictly Prohibiting Private Smuggling of Packages 98

The China Merchants Group believes that in the past, employees of various ships often smuggled packages privately. The group's freight revenue was affected, and the employees were also committing illegal acts. Moreover, the private smuggling of packages by a few unscrupulous elements affected all employees. Therefore, at the beginning of the rectification, the smuggling of packages was strictly prohibited. It is understood that the group is afraid that the employees of various ships may become lax over time, so it reiterated the ban the other day and ordered the supervisors of various ships to strictly inspect. If any goods are smuggled privately, 30% will be used as a reward, and the rest will be confiscated. The employees who smuggle privately will be punished according to law, so as to fundamentally eliminate smuggling.

Completion of New Luoxing Pagoda Pier; Director of Fujian Construction Department Arrives in Shanghai to Negotiate; Promoting Shanghai-Fujian Maritime Transport 102

The Luoxing Pagoda in Fuzhou, also known as Mawei, is an important route for ships to reach Fujian. Commercial ships from various places anchor there. Ships from Shanghai to Fuzhou, such as the Sanbei, China Merchants, Osaka, and Xin Chang'an shipping companies, have always only gone to Mawei, anchoring on buoys to load and unload goods and passengers. Due to water conditions, it was impossible to dock on the shore. Therefore, for decades, no pier had been built. In recent years, the Fujian Construction Department first built a wharf in Nantai and dredged the Hanjiang River to deepen the waterway, so that flat-bottomed ships with a draft of about ten feet can directly reach the Nantai wharf. However, larger sea vessels still cannot transport goods to Nantai. In order to promote freight transport in Fujian Province, the Construction Department raised huge funds to build an unprecedented large pier at the Luoxing Pagoda, deepening the waterway and using the latest construction methods. All warehouses and other facilities have been built. The pier is very large and can accommodate three sea vessels at the same time. The warehouse capacity is even larger. It was completed on October 3rd. On that day, the Shanghai Xinhua'an ship began docking at the new Luoxing Pagoda pier in Mawei, creating an unprecedented record in Fujian shipping history. In order to develop the Luoxing Pagoda pier business, since the transportation center is in Shanghai, Chen, the Director of the Construction Department, and Zhou Liangcai, the Director of the Luoxing Pagoda Pier Management Office, personally came to Shanghai to negotiate with various shipping companies in Shanghai and the leaders of various Fujian merchant groups. From now on, Shanghai-Fujian liners to Fujian, whether for unloading goods or boarding passengers, are requested to dock at the new Luoxing Pagoda pier, which can reduce the trouble and expense of using boats for unloading and transferring for shipping companies and passengers, and create a new era in transportation. Yesterday afternoon, representatives from various shipping companies and passenger companies discussed everything with Director Chen of the Construction Department and Director Zhou. (The picture shows the Xinhuan'an ship docking at the Luoxing Pagoda pier.)

Shanghai County Government Increases Public Arbitration Committee to Assess Land Price Tax for Newly Built Luoxing Pagoda Pier; Based on the Request of Representatives of Local Associations, Instructions Were Issued to Various District Bureaus Yesterday 103

The Shanghai County Government issued the following instructions yesterday: "According to the submission of Qin Xitian, Chairman of the Local Association, 'The submission is regarding the pre-collection of land price tax, the re-determination of land prices, and a special representative is raising an objection on behalf of all the property owners in the county, requesting that the Public Arbitration Committee be allowed to correct the errors in order to reassure the people and benefit tax revenue.' Our association proposed at a general meeting of members on September 27th of this year, 'How to realistically assess the land price in this county', and decided to conduct a zonal survey of actual land prices for comparison. The method is that in addition to the district head of each district, four people will be responsible for gathering township chiefs to inspect and report separately on purchase and sale deeds and income status in the past five years, and then each district head will submit them to our association to create a table and request the provincial county to correct them. While the district heads of each district were in progress, the county magistrate summoned the people for a joint talk on the 4th of this month. After the people of each district described the evaluation process and the resentment of the villagers, the county magistrate believed that this land price was unfair and inaccurate, and that the handling was hasty and needed to be corrected. According to law, property owners should raise objections, but it seems too cumbersome and causes disturbances for tens of thousands of property owners to request collectively. It was decided that our association would represent the property owners and submit a request to the county magistrate to order the Land Administration Bureau to temporarily increase the number of members on the original Public Arbitration Committee by ten, and to conduct an in-depth study with calm and composure, striving for appropriate prices, increasing or decreasing the current land prices separately, determining the standard for the tax amount, without hindering the provincial and county budgets and without increasing the burden on the farmers, so as to benefit both officials and the people. However, the procedures are complicated and cannot be handled in a short time. The autumn harvest is now underway, and the land price tax cannot be delayed because of this. It is proposed to collect the first installment of 50% of the tax first, and when the second installment is collected, the tax amount will be revised based on the revised land price. If the first installment is overpaid by more than 50% according to the new amount, the overpaid amount will be used to offset the tax for this installment, and if it is less than 50%, it will be paid in this installment. Such a flexible approach will comply with the law and the public opinion, which is truly a win-win situation. It is proposed to ask the county magistrate to approve the implementation before the land price tax is levied, and to distribute it to the various district offices so that the public can know it, so that the people's hearts can be stabilized and they can enthusiastically contribute. It is the blessing of the local area and the gift of the county magistrate. Therefore, in addition to ordering the submission to be noted, checking the implementation of the land price tax is the land policy set by the late Premier, and this county has been ordered to implement it on a trial basis, relying on the local talents to help and support it to be successful. The association suggested that ten members be added to the Public Arbitration Committee and properly arbitrated under the principle of not hindering the provincial and county budgets and not increasing the burden on the farmers. It is feasible for the association to recommend ten Public Arbitration Committee members who are property owners to the county for investigation. In addition to ordering the Land Tax Department to rush to start the levy procedure and the Land Administration Bureau to convene arbitration, the District Bureau is hereby notified to comply with this order.

The Shanghai West Minsheng Education Experimental Zone held a road construction meeting yesterday at 6:00 PM at the General Guidance Office on Zhongshan Road to discuss the construction of Minsheng Avenue. Chairman's Report

After formal greetings, Chairman Tang Maohuai first reported, stating briefly: "Dr. Sun Yat-sen said, 'The priority of construction is people's livelihood.' We call it 'Minsheng Avenue.' In particular, the eastern starting point of the road, from Zhongshan Road to Jinjia Lane, is the first section of the road. Previously, this zone had requested the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Public Works to allocate garbage and coal ash to widen and build it, but now it has sunk and become bumpy after a long time. Start of Discussion

Labor Service

Ministry of Finance Unifies the Issuance of Subsidiary Coin Notes, Provincial Banks Form Group Organizations, Provincial Banks or Local Banks Exchange Drafts and Redeem Subsidiary Coin Notes to Benefit Travelers 106

According to Xin Sheng News Agency, the Ministry of Finance has stipulated concrete measures for the unified issuance of subsidiary coin notes. Provincial banks or local banks have all complied. The Jiangxi Yumin, Zhejiang Local, and Jiangsu Farmer Banks have formed group organizations, exchanging drafts and redeeming subsidiary coin notes to facilitate finance. Details are as follows:

Ministry of Finance Unifies Subsidiary Coin Note Issuance

After the Ministry of Finance stipulated that subsidiary coin notes should be issued by provincial banks or local banks, it has stipulated measures for the sake of unifying subsidiary coin notes. Any provincial bank or local bank that prints subsidiary coin notes should state the reasons in detail and submit the design, type, quantity, scheduled manufacturing date, and completed manufacturing date of the subsidiary coin notes to the ministry for approval before manufacturing. As for the printing of subsidiary coin notes, it should be done by the ministry. Previously, the issuance of subsidiary coin notes by provincial banks and local banks was only approved by the provincial governments and had not been approved by the Ministry of Finance. The area of use was also limited to various places within the province.

Banks Issuing Subsidiary Coin Notes

Banks issuing subsidiary coin notes: (1) The Jiangsu Farmer Bank has been approved by the Ministry of Finance to issue subsidiary coin notes worth 3 million yuan, which will be used to withdraw the subsidiary coin notes previously issued by the Xuzhou Ping City Official Money Bureau, and they are already circulating in the market. (2) The 500,000 yuan of subsidiary coin notes previously issued by the Zhejiang Local Bank have been received by the Issuance Reserve Management Committee. A new request has been submitted to the Ministry of Finance for approval to issue 8 million yuan of subsidiary coin notes, and 3 million yuan have been approved and will be entrusted to a printing company for printing. (3) The subsidiary coin notes previously issued by the Jiangxi Yumin Bank have now been reported to the Ministry of Finance for record. (4) As for other provincial banks or local banks issuing subsidiary coin notes, they will resolutely apply to the Ministry of Finance for record according to law.

Local Bank Group Organizations

A reporter from Xin Sheng News Agency learned from banking circles yesterday that the Zhejiang Local Bank, Jiangxi Yumin Bank, Jiangsu Farmer Bank, etc., considering that the subsidiary coin notes of various banks are only allowed to circulate in various places within the province and are always rejected for use across provinces, which is very inconvenient for travelers, have decided to form group organizations for the sake of mutual communication. In the future, provincial banks or local banks will, in addition to exchanging drafts, redeem subsidiary coin notes for each other. It has been decided that the Jiangxi Yumin and Zhejiang Local Banks will first conduct a trial, and then gradually promote it to make it popular throughout the country.

In recent years, overseas Chinese compatriots living in the South Seas Islands have faced difficulties in making a living due to the impact of the global depression. Cabin Crew of the Tongzhou Wheel Reduced, Workers to Draw Lots Tomorrow: 113 People Reduced to 50 110

According to Xin Sheng News Agency, because the old Shanghai-Ningbo line's Xin Beijing ship owned by the British Taikoo Company was old, it was suspended this spring, and the Tongzhou Wheel was renamed Xin Beijing to replace it. However, because the Tongzhou Wheel's hull is narrow, it is difficult to accommodate the cabin crew of the two ships. (According to reports, the Tongzhou Wheel has 15 people, and the Beijing has 158 people, totaling 173 people. Since the old Xin Beijing was cut, all the workers have been working on the Tongzhou Wheel.) Therefore, the purser of the ship advocated reducing the number to 65 people. All the workers opposed this and requested the Seamen's Union Cabin Office to negotiate. Yesterday, the China Seamen's Union specially sent Secretary Wang Qi and Section Chief Wu Ya, together with Zhao Shijing from the branch, to negotiate with the company authorities. As a result, the company agreed to increase 15 more people, for a total of 80 people. (Among the 80 people, 15 old Tongzhou workers and 15 representatives of the Xin Beijing will not be cut. Among the remaining 143 people, 50 people will be drawn out for employment.) As for the dismissed workers, the purser will give each of them a severance payment of 83 yuan. At that time, both parties felt satisfied and declared a resolution. It was decided that a draw will be held at 10:00 AM on Monday at the cabin office to decide who stays and who goes. At the same time, the workers, feeling the pain of unemployment, decided that those who are drawn to continue to serve and the representatives will each contribute 90 yuan to distribute to the unemployed workers to maintain their livelihood.

"If Chiang's position collapses, Japan may have no way to find a counterpart for diplomacy towards China." "Although China has many dissatisfactions with Europe and America, the reason why anti-Japanese resistance has become an important issue is all because of the result of Japan's diplomacy towards China, which has caused even pro-Japanese elements in China to turn to anti-Japanese resistance."

Bizarre Argument: Japan's understanding of China should be fundamentally changed. Those who advocate the theory that the Chinese nation cannot be unified have an unparalleled adverse effect on diplomacy towards China. Zhu stated, "We believe that if there is no existence of Chiang Kai-shek, there is absolutely no possibility of discovering the relationship between the revival of Sino-Japanese friendship. His short-sighted diplomacy towards China is the cause of the current crisis." According to reports, Professor Konaka is an authority on Japanese political science and diplomatic history. Overseas Chinese Youth Aviator Xu Qixing Will Fly Back to His Homeland from Java 113

According to Central News Agency, Xu Qixing, a young Chinese aviator who made a long-distance flight between Java and the Netherlands last September, is now carrying out his long-distance flight back to his homeland from Java. The aircraft he is flying is still the small aircraft Walraven that he flew to the Netherlands before. He is accompanied only by his wife, Ms. Huang. His route is from Batavia, through Palembang in Sumatra, Singapore, Alor Star, Bangkok. If the weather is bad, he will not go to Siam but go directly to Saigon in Annam, heading to Hanoi, and then to Hong Kong, and then fly through Guangzhou and Xiamen to enter Beijing via Shanghai, to complete his long-distance flight from the capital of the Dutch East Indies to the capital of China. It is reported that Xu's flight is not making any records, but its purpose is to tour the motherland, investigate the recent situation of the aviation industry, and test the safety and speed of the aircraft made by the Dutch East Indies factory. He studied flying with Dutch officers in 1933, and because he had close contact with the technical staff of the Dutch East Indies aircraft factory, he had long had the desire to engage in the aviation industry. In 1934, he published his opinions on establishing an aircraft factory. When he went to the Netherlands last year, he went to the UK on the way and contacted various factories. As a result, everything was very satisfactory. This time he returned to China to investigate the aviation industry of the motherland as a reference. Xu is originally from Xiamen, an overseas Chinese student in Bondowoso, East Java. His family is quite wealthy, and he received a good education since childhood. He is proficient in English, Dutch, and other languages. He is only over thirty years old and is a promising youth in China.

Ministry of Railways Approves Six Grades of Waste Silk Yarn and Other Goods, Effective November 1st 114

The Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Bureaus received a business circular from the Ministry of Railways stating that the Shanghai Machine-Made National Products Factory Association had requested approval for the grades of six types of goods: waste silk yarn, cotton yarn, waste silk yarn piece ends, cotton yarn piece ends, and cotton and silk yarn piece ends. It was stated that their raw materials were all made of waste materials. After verification, it was approved that the waste silk yarn item should be charged according to the silk thread (made of waste silk) listed in the grading table, second grade. The cotton yarn and cotton and silk yarn items should be charged according to the wool yarn thread, second grade. The waste silk yarn piece ends should be charged according to the plain silk fabrics (Shandong silk), second grade. The cotton yarn piece ends and cotton and silk yarn piece ends should be charged according to the wool woven piece ends (ordinary), second grade. Public application will be implemented from November 1st of this year. This order has been forwarded to the Traffic Department by the bureau for compliance.

September Industrial Disaster Statistics Released by the Bureau of Social Affairs 115

The Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs Factory Inspection Office released the industrial disaster statistics for September. The total number was 107 cases, with 6 male workers and 1 female worker dead, and 79 male and 21 female workers injured. The causes of the disasters are listed below: (1) Power transmission device injured 2 males and 1 female; (2) Power-driven machinery injured 44 males and 11 females, and 1 female dead; (3) Electric shock injured 1 male; (4) Explosion killed 2 males; (5) Fire injured 1 male and 5 females, and killed 3 males; (6) High-heat objects and corrosive substances injured 10 males; (7) Collapse injured 4 males; (8) Handling of objects injured 15 males and 3 females, and killed 1 male; (9) Trampling or collision on objects injured 1 female; (10) Cause unknown injured 1 male; (11) Other causes injured 1 male. The total number of disasters decreased by one case compared to the previous month.

Medical Masterpiece: Photographic Reprint of Medical Records Examination 116

The book "Medical Records Examination" was written by Tanba Motoyasu of Japan. The entire book has 80 volumes and collects a total of 3,300 kinds of Chinese medical books. It almost comprehensively collects medical books from history to before the Daoguang period. Following the example of Zhu Yizun's "Classical Meaning Examination", each book first records the number of volumes, existence, and preface, and then Motoyasu's research. By examining one book, one can know the source and details of the book. By reading this book, the medical origins and schools of thought in China for thousands of years can be seen at a glance. The book was completed but not published. Last year, his country began to publish the original manuscript in photographic reprint. Each copy costs 120 yuan, which is not affordable for general readers. For the sake of promoting the inherent culture, the Chinese and Western Medicine Research Society of this city is reprinting the original book, combining four pages into one page. The font is still larger than size four, which not only preserves the original appearance but also eliminates the danger of typesetting errors. However, the original book has a vast number of subheadings, and it is quite difficult to find and check them. Therefore, the names of the medical books and the names of the authors collected in the book are separately compiled into a "Book Title Index" and "Personal Name Index", which are attached to the end of the book. It is not only convenient to check, but also one can immediately find out which book was written by which person and how many kinds were written by someone. All these practical advantages have exceeded the original book. Anyone who wants to study national medicine and study the history of Chinese culture must have it. Since the society issued the pre-order, the pre-orders have been quite enthusiastic. For example, Xu Senyu of the National Peiping Library pre-ordered as many as 18 copies at once, which shows how much it is valued by the cultural circle. Therefore, the 500 copies have long been exceeded. However, because some people have already purchased the "Medical Records Examination" published by a bookstore with a 30% discount, which is full of errors and completely unrecognizable, they have requested the society to add a few more copies to correct them. Therefore, the society will respond to their request to cope with it. There are still a few copies left for special sale. The book is printed on high-quality Lian Shi paper, divided into four large volumes, with magnetic blue paper covers and a specially made book box, which can be used as a shelf for hardcover books. The real price is 8 yuan, the special price is 85% off (plus 23 cents for postage per book). Schools and libraries that purchase them will get a 75% discount (limited to direct purchases from the society). The deadline is October 22nd. From October 23rd to November 22nd, the special price is 90% off, and schools and libraries get an 80% discount (method is the same as above). The real price will be sold after the deadline. There are not many books left, so purchase them as soon as possible. Those who have already sent a pre-order should pay the book price and pick up the books before November 22nd, otherwise it will be invalid. Publisher: Chinese and Western Medicine Research Society, No. 7, Lane 718, Yuyuan Road, Shanghai. Agents: Kaiming Bookstore on Fourth Malu and branches in various ports, Qianqing Hall Bookstore on Third Malu.

Seven Straw Houses Burned Down at Wangjia Burial Mound in the New West District 120

Wei Fuxin, 19 years old, from Funing, a rickshaw puller living in a grass shed at Wangjia Burial Mound in the New West District, accidentally started a fire while cooking at 11:00 AM the day before yesterday, which immediately burst through the roof. The wind fueled the fire, and it spread to the neighboring straw sheds around. After fire engines from various districts worked hard to extinguish the fire, seven straw houses were burned down. Subsequently, the New West District Police Station detained Wei Fuxin, the person who started the fire, for questioning.

The grandmother of Guan Jian, chief editor of Min Bao, and his brother Guan Jiu'an, Madam Zhang, suddenly suffered a stroke on the 11th of this month. News from Trade Associations 124

Artificial Silk Industry: Leading figures in the Shanghai artificial silk industry, including Pei Yuanding, Zhang Fuquan, and Ding Erchang, initiated the establishment of the Shanghai Artificial Silk Industry Trade Association. Preparatory work has been completed. Yesterday afternoon at 1:00 PM, the inaugural meeting was held at the association's location at No. 19 Chongrang Lane, Fuzhou Road. Over ten members were present. Representatives from the Municipal Party Headquarters, Mao Yun; the Social Affairs Bureau, Song Zhongqing; and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Yuan Hongjun, attended to supervise and guide the proceedings. Pei Yuanding, Sun Zhongshu, and Shen Laizhou were elected as the presidium, with Shi Yizheng as the recorder. The meeting commenced with customary formalities. Chairman Pei Yuanding first reported on the initiation and preparation process, followed by congratulatory remarks from the Party and government representatives. The meeting then proceeded to discuss the association's articles of association, which were revised and approved item by item. As a result of the election, Pei Yuanding, Zhang Fuquan, Shen Laizhou, Sun Zhongshu, Cao Lanru, Li Tingdong, Kang Xitao, Gu Xiyuan, and Yuan Jingbang were elected as executive committee members. Ding Erchang, Zhao Tingfu, and Sha Jingzhi were elected as alternate executive committee members. Subsequently, the general assembly approved the transfer of previously accumulated public funds to the association for safekeeping. In the evening, all executive committee members held a dinner and then convened their first meeting to allocate responsibilities.

Woolen Mill Industry: The Shanghai Woolen Mill Industry Trade Association previously convened a joint meeting of factory representatives to discuss price increases due to soaring raw material costs. Over twenty factory representatives attended, and Chen Xianben was elected as chairman, with Leng Bingnan as recorder. The following resolutions were passed: (1) In view of the recent surge in raw material prices, which has significantly impacted the industry's costs, measures should be taken to maintain capital. Resolved: Publish a public notice announcing a price increase of one dime per yard for camel wool. (2) The Ministry of Industry has approved the Sichuan Local Tax Bureau's report that camel wool sold in Sichuan Province, previously subject to a 45% landing tax, has now been reduced to 14%. Resolved: Notify the Huichang Company to comply. (3) The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau has approved the issuance of new certificates and instructed the dispatch of personnel to collect them. Resolved: Dispatch personnel to collect them. (4) The association's work is intensive, and funds are depleted. How should this be addressed? Resolved: Starting from November, membership fees will be doubled to maintain operations. Unanimously approved. The meeting adjourned after the resolutions were passed.

### Lu Furen Denies Writing Letters; Threatening Letters Have Identical Handwriting; Bi Songyou Receives Three Letters in a Row; Zhou Guohua Probably Doesn't Exist 125

Lu Furen, a 33-year-old man from Yangzhou, works as a cook in the kitchen of a shoe workshop run by his fellow townsman Guan Peiren at 523 Haichang Road, Zhabei, on the third floor. On the 10th, 15th, and 23rd of last month, he three times falsely used the name Zhou Guohua to write three threatening letters to Bi Songyou, a fellow townsman who owns a leather shoe workshop at 7 Guian Lane, Mintini Yin Road, French Concession, demanding 250 yuan, or else his entire family would be in mortal danger. If sincere, he was to send a letter to Zhou Guohua at the Tianshun Congee Shop, 523 Haichang Road, for negotiation, and so on. After receiving the letters, Bi reported to the French police. They prepared a letter in the same style and sent it by registered mail through the post office. Meanwhile, detectives from the police station, along with detectives from the Public Security Bureau, went to the Tianshun Congee Shop to lie in wait. They saw postal worker No. 579 deliver the letter to the Tianshun Congee Shop, where Lu accepted it. Lu then invited Guan Peiren, the owner of the shop, to go to the Taishan Temple Lower Courtyard at No. 4 Yongqing Lane on the same road to ask him to stamp the postal receipt. The detectives then arrested Lu, took him back to the Public Security Bureau, and brought him back to the French police station for interrogation and investigation. The Police Department has completed its investigation and confirmed that the handwriting on the threatening letters is identical to that of the defendant Lu Furen. Yesterday, Chen Shuoying, a judge from the Second Special District Court, continued the trial in the first criminal court. Gu Shouxi, a lawyer from the Police Department, explained the case and filed charges under Article 346 of the Criminal Code. When questioned, the defendant claimed that Zhou Guohua had asked him to receive the letter on his behalf and that he had not written any letters to the plaintiff to threaten and extort money. When asked where Zhou lived, he could not answer. The court verified the confession and announced the end of the debate, scheduling the sentencing for the 24th. The defendant was returned to custody.

Ningbo Sojourners Association in Shanghai Petitions for Relaxation of Bans on Logging and Gathering in Zhenhai 126

The Ningbo Sojourners Association in Shanghai submitted a petition to the Director of Civil Affairs of the Zhejiang Provincial Government and the Magistrate of Zhenhai County, stating: "Respectfully submitted, as per a joint letter from over twenty citizens of Zhenhai County, including Zhou Xutai, Yu Yunjiao, Wang Shangxiong, and Gu Jiaqiao, Zhenhai's four rural areas are mostly mountainous with barren soil. In addition to farming, the villagers also engage in logging and gathering firewood. In the past, private and government-owned mountains were open to the collection of both grass and firewood. Those poor people who had no fields to cultivate could make a living in this way. Since the county government designated the coastal mountain land along the river as protected forest, strictly prohibiting felling and issuing a general order stating that 'once afforestation has taken place on public or private mountain land, the mountains will be closed and the cutting of firewood will be prohibited.' The afforestation personnel of the fortress presented a document to the county government to ban logging, also including the words 'near the fortress area,' resulting in both a wide range of afforestation and the boundaries of the felling ban being further confused. The implementation measures for forest protection promulgated by the province were analysed in minute detail, the items were numerous and the network became denser. After closely examining the orders issued by the province and county, in a nutshell, it could be said that all mountains were banned and no firewood could be gathered. Will the villagers get used to the bans and obediently listen to orders? The people of the 20th century, in today's material evolution, will certainly find it difficult to live the life of the primitive era of drinking blood and eating fur, and they cannot break bones for fuel or cremate bones for cooking. Thus, if one man trips, eight mouths go hungry; if one corner of a mountain is closed, a thousand families starve. Will they be forced to engage in banned logging and gathering for a living? The distinction between prohibited and non-prohibited areas is unclear, the grass and forests are dense, and traps abound. Police and clerks extort and frame, and as long as an axe is held, a crime will be immediately committed. Moreover, burial in the plains is not allowed, and now the mountains are closed and cultivation is prohibited, so the dead will be left exposed and the coffins will be stopped forever. The ban above is strict and severe, and the situation below is painful and miserable. Alas, we have no complaints. The common people are wandering on the crossroads of life and death. Obeying orders is not possible, and disobeying orders is not possible. We feel trapped and do not know what to do. Since this year, poor people from several rural towns, such as Gaotang and Yongfeng, have been cutting pine branches on sacrificial mountains or mowing firewood on the foothills, resulting in more than a dozen people being detained and imprisoned one after another, and the cases in other rural areas that have been concluded and have not been made public are not included. The citizens live in the mountains and fields and see the suffering. The common people are weeping and speaking out, and it is difficult for us to remain silent. Therefore, we have something to offer and ask to pass it on to the authorities. We respectfully submit the following points based on our limited knowledge: (1) The afforestation area should be clearly demarcated. (2) The afforestation area should be allowed to cut firewood at any time. (3) The afforestation area should be allowed to harvest the grown trees at any time by the mountain owner. (4) The afforestation area should be allowed to cultivate and bury people at any time. In short, although the forest regulations have been promulgated for a long time, the implementation of afforestation is still a pioneering undertaking in our county. Moreover, the laws and regulations for protecting forests should take banning the felling of trees as the only principle. Now, they are exceeding the principle and cracking down on firewood, which is contrary to the original intention of the legislation. As the magistrate pointed out, if this continues for less than ten years, the old forest land will be transformed into thorny bushes, and logging will not be possible, and burial will not be possible. The survival and demise of both are like being hung upside down. The citizens have listed the above points, although the case involves changing historical policies and decrees, and is related to the government's major plans for consolidating the country and eliminating disasters, the general principles are still not in conflict. Your association maintains the homeland, and the six counties admire it. Therefore, we do not hesitate to speak out and offer our humble opinions. We respectfully request that you quickly send a letter to the relevant authorities and ask for a decree for the villagers. The future of the people's livelihood is deeply dependent on it. The association has received the above sentiments. After investigating the various points stated by the citizens, they are all essential. Therefore, we send this letter for your review and approval. Please instruct the Zhenhai County Government to make detailed regulations and announce them to the public for the benefit of all."

Prosecutor Investigates Assassination of Xuansheng Case; Takes Criminal to Perform On-Site 130

The Shanghai Public Security Bureau cracked the case of the assassination of a Japanese man named Xuansheng. The criminals Wang Zhensheng, Mao Yonghu, Zhao Yunhong, Jin Daohong, and women Wang Wangshi and Zhang Moshi, a total of six people, confessed to the crime. A pistol was seized and handed over to the local court for trial. It is reported that this case was originally investigated by Prosecutor Xie Lian. Now, Chief Prosecutor Zhu Huanqi believes that this assassination case involves international relations and has a political background with counter-revolutionary elements, and is not comparable to an ordinary murder case. In addition to personally supervising the investigation procedures, he also believes that the investigating prosecutor should be rich in experience and knowledge and carefully question the suspects. Because it is difficult for only one prosecutor to handle the case comprehensively, he has specially appointed Prosecutor Lei Binzhang to assist Prosecutor Xie in the investigation. After repeated interrogations, Wang Zhensheng confessed that he was instigated by Hua Ke to fire the gun and assassinate Xuansheng. He then threw the pistol into the garbage pile under the Hujia Wooden Bridge in Hongkou, and then fled back to the Changfa Inn. However, he claimed that the pistol was hidden by him, and Mao Yonghu took it out and shot Xuansheng, and then returned the pistol to him, and then he threw it away. The situation seemed quite unreasonable. However, Mao Yonghu confessed that the pistol was given to Mao by Li Ruiwu when they met at Zhao Yunhong's house, and Mao gave it to Wang Zhensheng, and Wang Zhensheng discarded it after the assassination. When Zhao Yunhong was questioned, he claimed that Mao Yonghu was his apprentice, and he was entrusted by Li Ruiwu, and Li was given a secret order by Hua Ke, and then Mao told Wang Zhensheng to carry out the assassination. The pistol used to kill the victim was recovered by the Public Security Bureau together with Wang from the garbage pile at the Hujia Wooden Bridge. The bullets were also very similar to the wounds of the deceased. However, after reading the confessions, it is still unclear who fired the gun. According to the circumstances, Wang Zhensheng is of course the person who actually carried out the crime. However, in order to confirm the truth, yesterday morning, Prosecutors Lei and Xie, accompanied by two bailiffs, escorted Wang Zhensheng in a car to the Hujia Wooden Bridge where the gun was thrown and the Gongmei Road where the murder occurred. Together with the police officers from the Linping Road Police Station of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, they performed an on-site demonstration, and then took him back to the court for detention.

In view of the upcoming opening of the Municipal Museum, and in order to enrich the content and promote national products, the museum has sent a letter to the China National Products Manufacturers Association, asking it to collect trademarks from various national product manufacturers and send them to the museum for display, so that visitors can recognize the trademarks of national products. After receiving the letter, the association has sent letters to various factories to comply. The original text is recorded as follows: "The Municipal Museum's letter of October 15th states, 'Dear Sirs, our museum has been preparing for a long time and will be opening soon. In order to enrich the content and promote national products, we plan to collect various trademarks of national products and display them publicly, so that visitors can recognize the trademarks of national products, which may be helpful in promoting national products. We have always known that your association is the leading organization of national product manufacturers, and we would like to ask you to collect national product trademarks and send them to our museum for display. We hereby request your approval and a reply.' We have approved this request. The museum's display of national product trademarks will encourage visitors to use national products, which is very beneficial to the national product movement. Moreover, the museum will be officially opened soon, and there will certainly be many visitors every day. All our national product factories should send their registered product trademarks directly to the museum at Funan Zuo Road, Municipal Central District, for display, so as to achieve effective publicity. This is what we hope for."

Jewish Man Murdered on Hart Road, Autopsy Performed; Abraham Had Considerable Savings; Landlady Yao Fang Discovers and Reports to Police 138

A Jewish man, Abraham (transliteration), 48 years old, was a vegetable vendor. One month ago, he rented a bungalow from Yao Fang, a local woman, at 57, Lane 644, Hart Road, for a monthly rent of nine yuan. On the night of the 15th and the morning before, he was attacked with a hammer and a wood-splitting axe and died. The murderer fled the scene. At 6:00 AM the morning before, Yao Fang was sweeping the street in the lane when she suddenly saw that the door of No. 57 was wide open. Suspicious, she went inside to investigate and found that the man had collapsed and died in the room. Her son, Yunsheng, reported the case to the Gordon Road Police Station, which dispatched Chief Detective Zhu Mengwei and Chinese and foreign detectives to investigate. Two murder weapons with bloodstains were found next to the body, and it was discovered that he had considerable savings. Therefore, the cause of the murder seemed to be for money. His body was sent to Hongen Hospital for a brief examination and then transferred to the Ferron Road autopsy center. Yesterday morning, the First Special District Court commissioned Prosecutor Song Genshan, along with forensic doctors Wei and Zhang, and clerk Wang Zuyi, to come to the center to examine the body. According to the report of the Chinese and foreign detectives, Yao Yunsheng, 37 years old, a local native, who works in printing and lives in the front bungalow in Lane 644, Hart Road, stated that the house where the deceased lived was his property and that he had rented it for one month and sixteen days and had paid him two months' rent. He had no family members. Yesterday morning, his mother went to sweep the floor in the lane and saw that his door was open, went inside, and found that he was dead. After obtaining the confession of Mr. Zhu, it was ordered that the deceased, the Jewish man Abraham, had died from injuries sustained before his death. The body was allowed to be collected for coffin burial by Aierjin Maai'er, the secretary of the Jewish Association. The fugitive murderer should be strictly apprehended by the police station in charge and brought to justice.

Shen's Family Lawsuit Over Property - Adopted Son Petitions for Co-residence with Adoptive Mother - Defendant Fails to Appear, Mediation Impossible - Plaintiff Should Pay Fee and File Lawsuit 140

Shen Xingquan, a local boy living in a bungalow in Shenjia Bang, at the intersection of Route Frelaut and Avenue Dubail in the French Concession, is eleven years old this year. His grandmother, Madam Shen Ma, has petitioned for mediation to co-reside with his adoptive mother, Shen Huang, who is also his aunt. The petition also addresses Huang's limited management rights but no ownership rights regarding the estate of her deceased husband, Miao Fa, and the inheritance of the estate of his adoptive father, Shen Miao Fa. The petition states that Shen Ma's husband, Shen Hairong, had two sons: the elder son was named Xitang, and the younger son was named Miao Fa. The elder son, Xitang, had one son, who is the petitioner, Shen Xingquan. Shen Miao Fa unfortunately passed away in 1928. His wife, Shen Huang, who is the defendant, initially stayed at home to uphold her commitment but left without saying goodbye after less than a year, taking away property deeds and assets, and has not returned since. Before his death, Shen Miao Fa, knowing he was seriously ill, personally designated the petitioner, Shen Xingquan, as his dual-lineage heir. After Shen Huang left, Shen Ma, as the grandmother, became Xingquan's guardian. It is also stated that since 1926, Shen Hairong had been unable to manage family affairs due to illness. His elder son, Xitang, took advantage of his father's confused state to demand a division of the family property, dividing all assets between Xitang and Miao Fa for management. If the two of them could maintain the family business, the petitioner's parents and Shen Shen, an aunt who is now eighty-two years old, could still rely on it for their livelihood. Unexpectedly, the elder son, Xitang, became frivolous and squandered all the property he received. The younger son, Miao Fa, unfortunately died young. The deeds to the five fen of field at No. 348, Zan Zi Wei, Er Tu, 27 Bao, Shangyi, and the nine fen, nine li, six hao of field at No. 380 in the same Wei, along with the documentation for three houses on the land, were all taken away by the defendant, Shen Huang. She then used her name to obtain a license from the Land Bureau. Shen Hairong, not understanding the law, was involved in lawsuits for five years and suffered adverse rulings. Shen Huang claims to be upholding her commitment, but under the circumstances, there is clear concealment. Therefore, the petitioner requests that the defendant be ordered to return home to co-reside, which is in line with both reason and law, it is claimed. According to the petition, the court, presided over by Judge He in Civil Division Four yesterday morning, attempted mediation. Only the petitioner and his lawyer appeared; the defendant did not appear. After the petitioner's side explained the reasons for requesting mediation, the court, noting the defendant's absence, declared the mediation unsuccessful and instructed the petitioner to formally file a lawsuit.

Ling Zhenchang - Marital Discord Escalates 143

Special First District Court Summons - Sheng Qunhe Embezzlement Case - Discrepancies in the Received Construction Costs - Defendant Retains Lawyer After Court Adjourns 144

The Wei Qingji Construction Company at 506 Zhongwang Lane, Ningbo Road, is owned by Wei Qingtao from Shaoxing, who hired Sheng Changan from Ningbo as manager. The company previously undertook the construction of the Shanghai Naval Hospital for the Navy Department, with over 20,000 yuan in construction fees still outstanding. Later, both Wei and Sheng passed away, and Wei's son, Nai Pu, took over the company. Sheng Changan's son, Sheng Qunhe, told Wei Naipu that the remaining construction fees from the Naval Hospital could not be obtained without his intervention with the director of the Jiangnan Shipyard, and that considerable expenses would be required. Wei Naipu then entered into a contract with him, agreeing to give him one-third of the recovered amount as a reward. Subsequently, Sheng recovered 10,000 yuan. After deducting the reward, he also donated 1,050 yuan to the Huangpu Military Academy Alumni Association, 200 yuan to the Fujian Pengfeng School, and 500 yuan for certain expenses, paying only 4,916 yuan to Wei, which was half of the 10,000 yuan. He also failed to collect the full amount. The remaining fees were to be paid by the Navy Department in eight installments. Recently, Wei sent a letter to the Navy Department to investigate and discovered various discrepancies on Sheng's part. Therefore, he filed a lawsuit against Sheng Qunhe in the Special First District Court, accusing him of embezzlement and requesting that he be punished under Article 335 of the Criminal Code, along with an accompanying civil lawsuit demanding the return of 11,684 yuan in national currency. The Special First District Court had previously summoned him, but the trial was suspended because the defendant's whereabouts were unknown. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Chuan Lin summoned him again in Criminal Division Eight. The plaintiff requested that the summons be entrusted to Fenghua and other places for service, which the court approved, ordering a rescheduled hearing. Immediately after the court adjourned, Sheng Qunhe suddenly retained lawyers Zhan Jifeng and Li Lin, who appeared in court. The judge informed them that the case had been rescheduled and instructed the defendant to appear in court for questioning at the next hearing.

Xu Yi's Private Prosecution - Dismissed and Incorrect Jurisdiction - Due to Narrowing of Scope of Private Prosecution - Changed to Suing the Prosecutor 145

Lawyer Xu Yi (also known as Jingxian) was previously sued by Li Quanshen (also known as Li Hairong), the manager of the Gen Taihe Flour Mill, in the Shanghai District Court and the Special First District Court, accused of forgery and other crimes. As a result, in the District Court case, Xu was sentenced to four months in prison, but the appeal was declared not guilty. In the Special First District Court case, Xu was sentenced to eight months in prison, but the appeal was rejected. After the bribery case involving Judge Tan Zhuohong of the District Court and lawyer Yang Shaopeng, Xu Yi believed that his case in the District Court was presided over by Tan and that the lawyer hired by Li et al. was Yang Shaopeng, and that Yang's fees reached 4,000 yuan. Therefore, he believed that Li was suspected of bribery. He then filed a private prosecution in the Special First District Court against Li Quanshen and Hu Zhetin (Cheng Linsheng's accountant, who signed the retainer agreement for lawyer Yang on his behalf) for bribery and false accusation, along with an accompanying civil lawsuit. The Special First District Court had summoned them several times, as reported in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, Judge Feng Shide continued the hearing in Criminal Division One. Judge Feng immediately declared to Xu Yi that the scope of the private prosecution had now been narrowed. Recently, the Supreme Court issued a precedent stating that bribery and perjury are both harms to national interests and cannot be privately prosecuted, only prosecuted by the prosecutor. Furthermore, you cannot present evidence in this case, and the High Court has also determined that the parts of the Tan case involving this case are not valid, so this court cannot accept it. As for your accusation of false accusation, it falls under the jurisdiction of the Shanghai District Court, so this court also believes that the jurisdiction is incorrect. Xu Yi then stated that he was adding an accusation against the defendant for violating Articles 125 and 132 of the Criminal Code, abuse of power, which concerns personal interests and should be accepted by your court. Judge Feng immediately stated that the provisions of that article only apply to officials who have the power to punish crimes. Since Li Quanshen is not an official, how can the crime of this article apply? Xu immediately stated that he would report the bribery and other matters to the prosecutor. Judge Feng then ruled that the part of the lawsuit against Li Hairong and Hu Zhetin for bribery was not accepted, and the accompanying civil lawsuit was rejected. The lawsuit against Li Hairong for false accusation, and the accompanying civil lawsuit, should be dismissed due to incorrect jurisdiction.

Criminal Case Arising From Gold Business - Both Sides Dispute Jurisdiction 146

Yang Weiren from Ningbo is an accountant at a money shop in Kobe, Japan, and Jiang Datian runs a grocery store in Kobe. Recently, Pan Liansheng, who opened a barber shop in Japan, and Xu Linshu, the manager of the money shop, retained lawyer Shi Qinghua to file a private lawsuit in the District Court against fraud and embezzlement. Because the crime took place abroad, according to Article 3 of the Criminal Code, it does not fall under the jurisdiction of this country. The court once ordered a suspension of the trial and awaited a further hearing by the court affairs meeting. Now, regarding the case of Xu Linshu suing Yang Weiren for embezzlement of over 6,000 yuan, the hearing has been rescheduled for the 21st of this month. Regarding the case of Pan Liansheng suing Jiang Datian and Yang Weiren for fraud under the pretext of doing gold business, Jiang Datian for defrauding 1,400 yuan, and Yang Weiren for defrauding 3,000 yuan, Judge Lu held a hearing. The defendants retained lawyer Xue Lisheng for defense. Regarding the issue of jurisdiction, lawyer Shi stated that although there are restrictions under Article 3 of the Criminal Code, this case involves bringing Japanese gold to Shanghai for sale. The crime occurred in Shanghai because this business was not conducted in Shanghai. Therefore, this country can accept it. The defendant stated that they were doing gold business, which was managed by Yu and Yang, and even they themselves were deceived. Litigation is currently underway in Ningbo. The court ordered the end of the debate, and the judgment will be announced on the 22nd.

Despicable Swindler - Cheats Luggage From the Poor - Lin Jinhuan and Gu Zhaolin are Victims - Wang Chunhua Seizes the Opportunity to Practice Deception 147

Lin Jinhuan and Gu Zhaolin, former servants in a Westerner's household on Route Cayol in the Concession, have been unemployed for a long time and are living in dire straits. They sought jobs everywhere through acquaintances, but without success. Wang Chunhua, a man from Hankou known to them, learned of their plight and claimed that his uncle owned a rice shop in Hankou and needed a clerk and an experienced bookkeeper. In addition to providing room and board, they would be paid more than ten yuan per month. He could introduce them. Lin and Gu, in their desperation, readily agreed and arranged to be led by Wang to board a Yangtze River steamer at a certain port in Hongkou around 2 PM the day before yesterday to go to Hankou. At that time, Lin and Gu brought a rattan suitcase, two hand baskets, and a bedding roll, worth a total of sixty to seventy yuan. Because the third-class fare was expensive, Wang negotiated with a cook and a second cook, surnamed Yang, on the steamer to allow the three of them to stay in the kitchen (commonly known as "traveling on the yellow fish") for only six yuan and fifty cents. After the agreement was reached, Wang deposited the luggage in the kitchen, claiming that the ship would set sail late at night. He said he would go to a barber shop to get a haircut, while Lin and Gu went to a bathhouse to bathe. In this short period of time, Wang secretly returned to the steamer and told the two cooks that he needed to pawn part of the luggage to raise money for the fare because it was not enough. The two cooks believed him and allowed Wang to take it away. When Lin and Gu returned to the steamer in the evening, only two empty hand baskets remained. They waited until late at night without seeing Wang, and became alarmed. They rushed to the customs police station to report the incident. The police sent detective Wang Haiquan to board the steamer for investigation and to apprehend the swindler.

He Wenying Sues on Behalf of Her Daughter - Yang Tianyu for Abandonment - Defendant's Address Unknown 148

Yang Tianyu, the former Commissioner of Opium Suppression in Fujian, met He Wenying, a woman from Hefei, Anhui (now 22 years old), in September 1933 and had a relationship with her, agreeing to marry her. However, He had already been promised to someone else, so she dissolved her engagement with her fiancé. Later, she discovered that Yang already had a wife and had also taken a woman surnamed Lin as a concubine. He insisted on marrying Yang, leading to a dispute. He then retained a lawyer and filed a lawsuit in the First Special District Court, accusing Yang of seduction and abandonment, along with an accompanying civil lawsuit, demanding alimony of 23,400 yuan. As a result, He lost the case. Subsequently, a settlement was reached, with Yang paying He 15 yuan per month for living expenses. On July 5th of this year, He gave birth to a daughter. Because Yang did not provide for the child's upbringing, and even failed to pay the 15 yuan monthly living expenses as stipulated in the previous settlement, he has now retained lawyer Shi Jiutang and filed a lawsuit in the Special First District Court against Yang Tianyu for abandoning the child, requesting that he be punished under Article 294 of the Criminal Code, along with an accompanying civil lawsuit, demanding the payment of education and other expenses, totaling 9,300 yuan. Because Yang is currently in the capital, it is requested that the summons be sent to his brother, Yang Tianying, at No. 66 Tianjin Road for forwarding. The court approved the request and issued a summons, which was delivered to Yang Tianying, but Yang Tianying refused to accept it. Therefore, yesterday afternoon, when Judge Chuan Lin held the hearing in Criminal Division Eight, the defendant did not appear. Judge Chuan Lin then instructed the plaintiff to ascertain the defendant's correct address and report it, and the case was postponed for a rescheduled hearing.

Changsha, 16th - The Central China Sports Promotion Association held its second representative meeting on the 16th, resolving: (1) to suggest that the National Sports Association prepare for participation in the World Games in 1940; (2) starting from the 6th Central China Games, to abolish the overall championship system; (3) future chief referees must be hired from outside the four provinces and be sports experts not from the four provinces; (4) to add the education directors of the four provinces as ex-officio members of the association's executive committee; (5) the secretary-general shall prepare and elect the next term of officers by correspondence within three months.

At 1:00 PM, the closing ceremony was held at the 49th Standard. He hoped for even greater progress and more promotion in the future, so that the people of the nation would become athletic, militarized, and proficient in national arts (Wushu), promoting and carrying them forward. Everyone should take responsibility for reviving the nation to save it from peril. Next, Zhang Zhijiang delivered an address, encouraging everyone with the eight characters of "peace, struggle, avenge, resist." After the address, the chief referee reported the results of various events, and prizes were distributed, with athletes cheering and dispersing. Donghua Wins Western Police 2-1

Western Police attacked first, but were immediately besieged by Donghua. Wu Binghao's shot missed. Donghua was once in danger, but fortunately, Sun Baoqing defused the danger. Donghua repeatedly launched attacks. Although the ball was mostly at Donghua's feet, they gained nothing. The first half ended 0-0. After the break, Donghua's offensive was very strong. In the eighth minute, Wan Xianghua single-handedly went straight in, dribbled past Pei Daoke, and shot from 15 yards, scoring the first goal. Western Police desperately counterattacked. Bao Tai kicked the ball into the goal, making it 1-1. Less than a minute had passed since Donghua's goal. In the twelfth minute, Wan Xianghua received a pass from Sun Jinshun and advanced alongside Wu Binghao, scoring a goal, making it 2-1. Near the end, Donghua's Sun Jinshun took a penalty kick, which bounced out off Aite Menz, and the game ended 2-1.

Education News

Recent Years of National Higher Education: More Students Admitted to Science-Related Fields, Fewer to Humanities Fields 167

The Ministry of Education has compiled statistics comparing the fields of study of newly admitted students in national colleges and universities in recent years, which are excerpted below:

(Explanation) (1) In the 20th year, science-related fields accounted for 30.7% of the total, and humanities-related fields accounted for 69%. (2) In the 21st year, science-related fields accounted for 36.6%, and humanities-related fields accounted for 63.4%. (3) In the 22nd year, science-related fields accounted for 39.8%, and humanities-related fields accounted for 60.2%. (4) In the 23rd year, science-related fields accounted for 45.97%, and humanities-related fields accounted for 54.03%. (5) In the 24th year, science-related fields accounted for 51.18%, and humanities-related fields accounted for 48.82%. In the past nine years, the number of students in science-related fields has increased year by year, while the number of students in humanities-related fields has decreased, which is also a result of adapting to environmental needs.

West Cheng Elementary School: Grand 30th Anniversary Celebration, Continuing Today 173

West Cheng Municipal Elementary School held its 30th anniversary celebration yesterday. The celebration ceremony was exceptionally grand and enthusiastic. Over two thousand guests attended. A report on the grand occasion is as follows: At 9:00 AM yesterday, the entire faculty and student body of the school gathered on the large playground. After the flag-raising ceremony, they entered the auditorium to hold the commemorative ceremony. First, Principal Chai Zifei reported on the purpose of the meeting. Then, Director Pan of the Social Affairs Bureau delivered a speech, stating that the school has achieved its current grand scale through thirty years of effort. He expressed his hope that all faculty and students will make use of this superior environment, continue their past efforts, and strive for even greater achievements. He also stated that the administrative authorities are willing to do their utmost to support the development of the school. Tao Baichuan, the representative of the Municipal Party Headquarters, told stories of the actual lives of children in Europe and America to encourage the children to develop qualities and habits such as courage, integrity, and politeness, so that they can become useful and powerful citizens. Next, guests Jiang Jianbai, Yao Minghui, Zhao Lüqing, Wang Zhuangfei, and others successively gave speeches, offering sincere words of encouragement. Finally, student representatives such as Ye Lanruo gave congratulatory speeches, and the ceremony concluded with cheers from the faculty and students. Yesterday, the school held an all-day exhibition of achievements, with over ten thousand items of work displayed in fifteen rooms. In addition to the regular work of each subject, there was a separate room for each of the four groups (kindergarten, lower grades, middle grades, and upper grades) showcasing unit teaching achievements. Both the quality and quantity were rich and beautiful. At 2:00 PM, a variety show was held with twenty-four performances. In addition to the performances by the school's children, four other schools (Wan Zhu, Shang Wen, Wu Zhong, and Wu Xiao) participated. The atmosphere at the venue was extremely lively. From 7:30 PM in the evening, the Xin'an Traveling Troupe screened educational films at the school. The films were produced by Mingxing Film Company and the Central Propaganda Committee, and the plots were highly educational. Today is the second day of the celebration. At 9:00 AM, the alumni association founding meeting will be held. A luncheon will be held for alumni at noon, with a cost of one yuan per person. Over three hundred alumni and former faculty members have registered to attend. The achievement exhibition and variety show will continue according to the program of the first day, and the public is welcome to visit the school for guidance.

Commercial News

Yarn and Cotton: Marked Yarn Finds New Five-Year High 178

Warehouse yarn inventory only 9,000 bales remaining; October rises to $220, still cheaper than spot by $6-7.

The yarn market's upward trend has returned, as the spot yarn situation tightens, with factories reporting stockouts. As a result, warehouse yarn is extraordinarily sought after, with only about 9,000 bales remaining. Prices are rising steadily, and market sentiment is excited. Marked yarn has followed, rising accordingly. However, compared to spot market prices, it is still cheaper by $6-7. The October yarn contract closed at $220, finding a new five-year high, surpassing the July 13th forward yarn price of $219.80.

Da Feng and Others: Wholesale Purchasing

The marked yarn market opened, and recent months have seen spot yarn unusually scarce, with prices exceeding marked yarn by $7-8. Therefore, buyers flocked in, and the market remained firmly up by $1.00 to $1.20. Forward contracts experienced heavy selling pressure from a major player and securities firms, falling by $0.08-0.09. The second session was nearly flat with the previous one. At the close of the third session, reports indicated that spot yarn sales, while better than the previous day, still saw rising prices. Market sentiment was revitalized, and all months rebounded. Yuda, Hexing, Dachangcheng, and other large players sold heavily, while Dafeng, Gengfeng, Ruida, Shenji, Changfeng, and Dachang Xiecheng made wholesale purchases. As a result, near-term contracts rose by $1.30-$1.40 from the previous day's close, and forward contracts rose by $0.02-0.05. The afternoon session opened with a tight market, as yarn sales were lively and factories had no spot yarn to supply. Short sellers panicked, and prices jumped by $1.00. After the second session, they rose steadily. Hexing continued to sell heavily. As a result, all months rose by $1.20-$2.10 from the morning close. Sales were Hexing 13,900 bales, Deda 1,200 bales, Zhenda 1,500 bales, Dachangcheng 1,500 bales, Tongfu 1,300 bales, Changyu 1,300 bales, Renfeng 3,300 bales, Changfeng 1,650 bales, Dachang 1,050 bales, and Xincheng 3,400 bales. Purchases were Dafeng 1,950 bales, Gengfeng 5,150 bales, Jifeng 1,700 bales, Ruida 1,450 bales, Shenji 4,750 bales, Changfeng 4,500 bales, Xiecheng 2,550 bales, Dachang 1,850 bales, Shengyuan 2,000 bales, Yicheng 4,000 bales, Wang Taixing 1,300 bales, Hengyi 1,050 bales, and Tongji 1,100 bales. The day's high and low prices are listed on the left.

Observations on Japanese and American Silk Markets: Apparent Significant Increase in US Hosiery Consumption; Rumors of Japan Organizing Large-Scale Raw Silk Company 192

Although recent transactions in New York raw silk have not been brisk, US hosiery manufacturers have been actively purchasing. Recently, 20-22 denier raw silk has been in short supply, while there is reluctance to purchase futures, mainly due to Italy shipping 20,000 to 25,000 bales of raw silk to the US in this season (July 1936 - June 1937). It is reported that a small amount has already been delivered to factories for use. The buyers are mostly warp knitting mills, and the sales of silk fabrics are currently brisk, leading to strong futures prices, but this is mainly driven by speculation. The rayon trade is also active. As for the supply and demand issues in the US market this season, estimations based on the current situation are as follows, making it easier to predict future price trends:

Japan's silk production capacity: 440,000 bales (decrease of 25,000 bales compared to last season) + 20,000 bales (released from government's last season's inventory)

Japan's total: 460,000 bales + 101,000 bales (increase of 20,000 bales compared to last year) + 21,000 bales (Italian export volume)

Total: 581,000 bales - 110,000 bales (for European consumption) = 471,000 bales (available for US consumption)

Based on the above estimate, the consumption volume for the 12-month season is 472,000 bales, which is not a significant increase compared to the previous season's consumption of 456,000 bales. Furthermore, the first four months of the last season, which saw extremely strong consumption, were not as robust as this season. The consumption volumes for July, August, and September this season were 36,658 bales, 42,016 bales, and 45,709 bales, respectively, with an estimated 45,000 bales for October, totaling 169,383 bales in these four months. Subtracting 169,383 bales from 472,000 bales leaves 302,000 bales, which can supply US consumption for eight months. Based on the above estimate, if accurate, the average monthly consumption would be 38,000 bales. In previous years, this number would have been considered insufficient, but the average monthly consumption during the same period last year was only 34,700 bales, so careful consideration is necessary. Furthermore, compared to 34,700 bales, there would be a surplus of 3,300 bales per month, totaling 26,400 bales in eight months. Although the above estimates are predictions, they are likely not exaggerated. The increase in production in both Italy and China this year is expected, and the consumption volume in Europe and the US is not expected to deviate significantly. The only difference lies in the increase or decrease in US consumption. The US hosiery industry's consumption has increased compared to the previous season, which is very clear. It is expected that the silk market will become more active in the next eight months, so prices are not expected to decline significantly. However, there is also a disturbing piece of news that may pose some potential risks to the future of the silk market, namely, Japan's Seiyukai party plans to establish a large-scale Japanese raw silk company. There is much speculation about this rumor, but the consensus is that the intention is to dominate the Japanese silk export industry. If this organization is established, the existing exporters will inevitably be forced to dissolve, and the future silk market may become unstable.
