Children's Section

Start with Effort, Results Will Surely Be Good 194

— Yang Chunlu

It has been over a month since school started. Children are once again finding happy lives in the schoolyard. But you must remember the saying "Be careful in starting your studies." At the beginning of this semester, you should put in more effort, explore deeply, and study carefully. Sweet fruits are waiting for you to taste.

Children! Don't think that the semester has just started, and there is plenty of time in the future, and there will be many days to study hard! You must know that time flies, and a semester will pass in the blink of an eye. We can only seize the present and work hard in time to get a satisfactory start.

Children who have participated in races will surely remember that in 50-meter or 100-meter races, when the gun sounds, if you don't immediately start running and rush forward, you will fall behind. Studying is the same. You must have a good start to have good results!

Children! It's time. Work hard! Strive! A satisfactory victory will surely belong to you!

Teeth 195

— Zhen

In recent days, Min'er has been suffering from toothache, making it inconvenient to eat and talk, causing him great suffering. He wondered why the toothache happened so that he could prevent it later.

"Brother, toothache is more uncomfortable than any other disease. Why does it happen?"

"This is because food is stuck in the gaps of the teeth for a long time, causing it to rot and turn sour, gradually peeling off the enamel and dentin, and affecting the nerves, which causes toothache."

"What is enamel? What is dentin?"

"I have to briefly explain the composition of teeth to you: Our teeth are divided into incisors, canines, premolars, and molars. The composition of the teeth: (1) The part of the tooth that is exposed outside the gums and can be seen is called the crown. The crown is made of enamel, which is as hard as stone and forms the outer layer of the tooth. Enamel is the hardest part of the human body. (2) The part of the tooth that is embedded in the jawbone by the gums is called the root. Incisors and canines have only one root, while molars have two or three roots. The root is composed of dentin. In the middle of the dentin is a pulp cavity, which is full of blood vessels and nerves."

"The shape of the teeth is different, so they are divided into the incisors, canines, premolars, and molars that I just told you about. Incisors are like small chisels, so they can bite off food. Canines are conical and can crush hard food. Premolars and molars are both mortar-shaped and can grind food further."

"How many teeth do we have? Are the teeth of young children the same as ours?"

"I have about thirty-two teeth, because I am an adult. There are about eight incisors, four canines, eight premolars, and twelve molars. Your teeth do not have a definite number, because you are not yet an adult. The teeth of young children have only twenty, ten in the upper jaw and ten in the lower jaw. However, the teeth that come out in childhood are called baby teeth. When they are about seven years old, the baby teeth will fall out one after another, and new teeth will grow in successively. By the time they are about twelve years old, the baby teeth will be completely replaced. These newly grown teeth are everyone's permanent teeth, so we must protect them well."

Make a Beautiful and Lively Goldfish 196

— Zheng Yun

A goldfish seller came outside the door, prompting Xin'er to force his father to buy one. Dad nodded, thought for a while, and said happily:

"Xin, if we buy a few of these goldfish and raise them in a fish tank, it may be difficult for them to survive for long. Now I have a beautiful, lively, and never-dying goldfish. Would you like to have it? But you have to use your hands."

"Yes, I am willing to do anything to get a goldfish."

So Dad began to tell him how to use his hands and how to get a beautiful and lively goldfish:

Take an egg and use a knife to open a small hole at each end, so that the yolk and white inside can flow out together. Then use drawing paper to cut out a fish tail. Separately use a thread, one end tied to the base of the fish tail, and the other end passed through the larger hole of the eggshell and out of the smaller hole. Then make a knot slightly larger than the small hole; in this way, the goldfish's body shell is made.

The second part of the work: Apply red paint on its body shell. After it is dry, use an ink brush to draw the surface of the fish. At that time, you can inject half of the sand and mud inside the eggshell into the small hole at the base of the fish tail to maintain stability when it is put into water. Then you can use melted wax to seal the small holes on both the large and small ends of the egg. In this way, the goldfish is already made. (See the picture)

When playing: Use some soap to stick under the base of the fish tail. Put the goldfish in a water basin. By the power of the soap, the goldfish can slowly swim forward; at the same time, the fish tail can also slowly sway. It looks like a beautiful and lively goldfish is looking for its companions!

Xin'er followed his father's instructions, prepared all the materials, and started to make it. Sure enough, now he has a beautiful, lively, and never-dying goldfish.

The Lesson of Autumn Insects 197

— Chen Tiewu

In the grass, a rustling sound,

Calling "brother" all night long;

It's because: ——

Foreign goods are dumped in our market,

Local goods are no match for inferior goods;

Reluctant to part with: ——

The Mexican dollar flowing abroad.

The weaver cricket, the sound of the loom rings,

Working hard under the stars and moon;

It's because: ——

Our country's production is too backward,

The economy is becoming more and more alarming;

Reminding me: ——

Self-sufficiency is the most glorious.

The little cricket, with its chest puffed out,

Killing each other without stopping;

Until finally: ——

When the autumn wind rises, they all perish,

No chirping is heard again;

Reminding me: ——

To avoid foreign aggression, we must first quell internal strife.

Science Questions

Why can ships sail in water? Why can airplanes move forward in the air? 198

— Yan Maode

Children! You always have a feeling, why can ships sail in water? Why can airplanes move forward in the air? What is the principle behind this? Perhaps few of you children know the reason, so let me give a simple explanation:

People do not have automatic ability, that is, people must be directed by others. In other words, people's actions are passive rather than active. Newton told us in the first law: "All objects, if not acted upon by an external force, will remain at rest forever, and objects in motion will continue to move at a constant speed forever. This relationship is also called the law of inertia." Therefore, because objects have inertia, an external force must be applied to make them move:

If a person pushes an object with force, because the object has inertia, it seems that the object has the force to push back, and its force is equal to the force used by the person. Therefore, ships can sail in water and airplanes can move forward in the air by using this reaction force. When a ship is in the water, it is propelled by oars rowing the water, which creates a reaction force that makes the ship move forward. Steamships use propellers, which consist of two or more metal plates mounted around a shaft. The engine causes the propeller to rotate, pushing water or air backward, and the reaction force of the body propels the propeller forward, moving in the direction of the rotating shaft, thus pushing the ship forward. Airplanes also use propellers. When the propeller rotates, it pushes air backward, causing the airplane to move forward; at the same time, the resistance under the wings is the pressure of the wind. Furthermore, the tail has two rudders, one is a horizontal rudder, which controls the ascent and descent of the body, and one is a vertical rudder, which controls the direction of the body's left and right movement. This is how airplanes fly.

Returning from the National Boy Scout Grand Review 199

— Xiong Feng

Our hope has finally been realized. The Second National Boy Scout Grand Review and Jamboree, which had been postponed so many times, finally showed its magnificent appearance in our capital on Double Ten Day.

What left the deepest impression on our minds at this conference was the spirit of President Chiang, what excited us the most was the air defense performance, what made us feel the greatest was the united strength of our Boy Scout, and what interested us the most was the construction of the campsite.

On the first day, I ran to the headquarters and saw a picture of President Chiang commanding the Boy Scouts on horseback erected in front of the door. This great picture made us feel excited. On the second day, the President flew to the campsite in an airplane at low altitude to welcome us. The sound of welcome rose from all sides. Later, we learned that the President had just arrived in Beijing from Jiangxi and took the opportunity to inspect the campsite. When the campsite movie was playing, the first one was to wish him a long life, which told us about President Chiang's great achievements. His heroic spirit was deeply imprinted in our minds. When we got up the next morning, the first thought that came to mind was President Chiang's heroic demeanor! On the day of the review, he wore a uniform adorned with gold stripes, showing his special majesty. When he walked past us, if it were not for the solemn review ceremony, I would have cheered madly.

More than 10,000 representatives of Boy Scouts from all over the country gathered in our capital, which shows that we are united and ready to serve the country. We camped together, played together, participated in labor service, and held campfire rallies and lantern parades. In particular, the representatives from the four northeastern provinces also participated in our team, which further stirred our enthusiastic emotions. Young people have active minds, passionate blood, enterprising spirit, and vigorous vitality. Everyone says that young people are the new cells of the country and the new bloodline of the nation. This grand gathering shows a new force for the revival of our country.

The construction of the campsite interested us the most. The sundial in the center of the campsite, the artificial thermometer, and the weather report flags were all very new designs. The layout of the campsites in each unit was even more novel and magnificent. Some places looked like a small garden, while others looked like an arsenal. I believe that the representatives who participated in this conference must have gained a lot of experience and knowledge about the layout of the campsite.

Now many new friends we have made will soon be separated. I hope that the third conference will be held in the near future. Some people say that the third conference will be held in Liaoning. We hope that this statement can be realized.

—This article is a report sent by a Boy Scout to the Chinese Boy Scout Self-Help Society. It is published here to inform the Boy Scouts and readers who did not participate in the conference—Editor

Hanging Objects with Burnt Thread 200

— Xu Xiaoting

I took a long piece of burnt thread, tied one end to the top of an object, and the other end to a small toy, such as a tumbler, or four or five coins. When it is suspended in the air, use fire to burn it. Although the thread turns to ash, it does not break, and the object is still suspended in the air and does not fall off. This is a very interesting little game.

The method is to soak a two- or three-foot-long cotton thread in salt water overnight, then take it out and dry it. Then, use egg white to apply it to the thread. After it is dry, you can use it to play. The strangest thing is that when the thread turns to ash, we can slightly touch it with our fingers. At this time, the thread has actually turned into ashes, but it can still hang objects without breaking when playing. This is very magical. Children, why not try this simple and easy-to-make game in your spare time?

The Travels of a Dandelion 202

— Zhou Rubo, Shanghai Municipal Songxue Elementary School

Autumn has arrived, and our traveling team will soon be active again!

Last night, we prepared everything; today we bid farewell to our parents and all our relatives and friends, and set off on a journey to the southeast. We are riding on Mr. Wind's ship. At first, we arrived at China's largest commercial port - Shanghai. When I passed through Shanghai, I was very scared. Originally, the Whampoa River was full of foreign warships. Their soldiers were wearing new-style military uniforms, and all the new-style weapons were in their hands, which made me dare not stay. We then went to a lively place to travel. This trip scared me even more. Because when we passed that place, only those blue-eyed, blond-haired foreigners were building forts, piling sandbags, and digging trenches. We did not know what the reason was: why would foreigners live in China? Finally, I realized: it turned out to be a concession. I was scared and dared not stay, so I looked for a quieter place to go. Finally, I found a peaceful place to live, in the garden of a sincere and simple farmer. There was nothing in this garden that would harm me, and it was quiet and refreshing. So I settled down, and I will live here permanently, as my base, to maintain my life and raise my future generations.

The Seven Sisters of the Mountains (4) 203

— Xin Qing

They continued searching day after day, but the couple remained untraced. The neighbors put aside their own work and patiently cleared away the snow piled up on the mountain paths around Lantai day after day. However, after four or five days, they were still nowhere to be found. Finally, they used many dogs to lead the searchers to distant places beyond the mountain paths. Suddenly, a loud shout rang out from the top of a jagged cliff, and they knew that the lost couple had been found. Shanlan Ge Lin was lying stiffly there, covered in her husband's coat, having obviously died long ago. George Ge Lin's body was found at the bottom of a rock, and judging by his hunched posture, it was clear that he had fallen from the mountain and died instantly. The neighbors surmised that the couple must have been lost in the heavy snow and fog that night, and thus walked further and further until they reached the dark, jagged cliff. George Ge Lin had taken a few steps forward, trying to see if there was a path ahead, but he accidentally stepped off the edge of the cliff and fell. Shanlan probably didn't know what had happened and was still standing in place, desperately calling out to her husband, but in the deep snow of that night, no one in Lantai could have heard her. When she became hoarse and exhausted and could no longer move, she lay there waiting for her husband and eventually froze to death. According to those familiar with the couple, the pitiful Shanlan must have been worried about the many children at home at that time, and her anxiety urged her husband to hurry back, which caused him to lose his composure. If he had been alone, this disaster would never have happened. The brave little Anne Ge Lin stayed at home to take care of her six younger siblings, calmly waiting for her parents to return. In the end, she hesitated and then went out alone in the snow to look for them. This clearly demonstrated the military heritage she inherited from her father, and it was truly remarkable. The British poet William Wordsworth's sister, Dorothy, visited little Anne Ge Lin and listened to her recount everything that had happened, considering it to be a very precious story.

In a lovely spring, the Ge Lin couple was buried in the St. Swale cemetery in Cockermouth. William Wordsworth wrote a poem in their memory. After the funeral, the neighboring farmers all volunteered to adopt the seven orphans as their godchildren. The twin girls remained together, and the Gansling family adopted them. Little Anne Ge Lin, although separated from her siblings, wanted to live comfortably with her parents' friends. People near and far heard about this story and donated money, sending it in droves. Queen Charlotte and her princesses were also moved by little Anne Ge Lin's bravery and bestowed a generous sum of money as consolation, which was distributed to the orphans. People everywhere followed suit, and money came flying in like snowflakes. However, Dorothy Wordsworth refused it all because she thought that if the orphans received too much money, they would lose their ambition when they grew up, which would greatly affect their future.

Commentary

"Establishment of Liaison Between Chinese and Japanese Newspapers" 204

— Liang Boxun

Since the newspapers in Beijing and Shanghai published common opinions and beliefs amidst the tense Sino-Japanese relations, and warned the people of the whole country and the Japanese government and the public, the press circles in various places have responded one after another, which shows that the people of our country have the same feelings about the current Sino-Japanese problem. On the Japanese side, at this time of tense Sino-Japanese relations, there are also remarks that are worth our attention. This is the text recently published by Mr. Ishibashi Tanzan, the chief writer of the "Toyo Keizai Shimpo": "Hope for the Establishment of Liaison Between the Press Circles to Adjust Sino-Japanese Relations" (the general idea of ​​the article is published in the "Shen Bao" on October 13). In this article, Mr. Ishibashi criticized the Japanese newspapers for turning a deaf ear to the joint telegram issued by the newspapers in Beijing, Shanghai, and Guangdong-Hankou; and pointed out that "Japanese newspapers are good at destroying the relationship between Japan and foreign countries, and have no intention of maintaining international relations; Japanese newspapers now hold extreme patriotism, and have almost become a diplomatic organ of bureaucratic politics." Regarding the future of Sino-Japanese negotiations, he also expressed deep concern, saying that "if Japan's negotiation strategy proves to be clumsy, the danger of the Twenty-One Demands will almost be re-enacted, and Japan's misfortune will be even greater than China's! He also said that Foreign Minister Arita's declaration on September 28 "is clear in blaming others, but ignorant of blaming oneself." If this kind of comment is spoken by the people of our country, it may be pointed out as a manifestation of "anti-Japanese thinking," but now the person who made this statement is Mr. Ishibashi, a famous figure in the Japanese press, I wonder what the people of "friendly countries" will say about this. At the same time, Mr. Ishibashi sincerely hopes in this article that the newspapers of the two countries will establish understanding, "on the one hand, Chinese newspapers will not publish anti-Japanese news, and on the other hand, Japanese newspapers will not make malicious criticisms of China, and believe that if the newspapers of the two countries establish a liaison, it can promote the improvement of relations between the two countries." If this kind of hope can become a reality, of course, it is also what we are happy to hear. However, based on past facts and the current situation, we still have a few opinions to put forward for discussion here.

First, I don’t know what the so-called "anti-Japanese news" refers to. If it is said that Chinese newspapers publish news about a certain country's invasion of our land, publish the patriotic actions of our people, and express opinions on protecting the integrity of our country's territory and sovereignty, that is to exclude a certain country, then it is no different from prohibiting Chinese newspapers and Chinese people from loving China. We can never accept that. Naturally, the so-called "extreme patriotism," patriotism that invades neighboring countries to enrich oneself, has always been despised by Chinese newspapers and Chinese people, but the independence of the Chinese nation and the sovereignty of the country must be unanimously supported; if a country carries out the plundering of our country's territory and rights, and wants to force our entire people to be dominated by it, then our 400 million compatriots will surely hate it, hate it, and fight it to the end! This kind of performance of fighting for national independence and the spirit of fighting for the integrity of national territory and administration should be praised by the whole world and absolutely preserved by our people. If a strong neighbor is embracing "extreme patriotism" and infringing on our country's sovereignty, and wants us to abandon this great spirit of fighting for national independence, is it not a strange thing!

Second, if Chinese newspapers really publish the so-called "anti-Japanese news," then we should ask the Japanese people and general enlightened people such as Mr. Ishibashi to pay attention to the source of this so-called "anti-Japanese news." The Chinese nation is not a nation that makes a career of invading others, and absolutely does not want to exclude foreigners "anti-Japanese" for no reason. If we want to regard the Chinese people's upright and aboveboard patriotic movement as "anti-Japanese" behavior and regard it as an obstacle to improving relations between China and Japan, then the Japanese people and the general enlightened people should consider whether the Japanese government and soldiers have actions that infringe on the integrity of China's territory and administration, and whether they really use the "principle of equality" to adjust the relations between the two countries. If the factual answer is a "yes" and a "no," then the deterioration of Sino-Japanese relations and the disharmony of the feelings of the two major nations of China and Japan are all the responsibility of Japan; and the Japanese people and the general enlightened people, if they want to improve Sino-Japanese relations, they should also find ways to correct the attitude of the Japanese military and political authorities towards China.

Third, we are not in a position to comment on Japanese newspapers. However, if what Mr. Ishibashi said is all true, that is, Japanese newspapers are "holding extreme patriotism," "good at destroying the relationship between Japan and foreign countries," and "diplomatic organs of bureaucratic politics," then if we want to "establish a liaison between Chinese and Japanese newspapers," we should first pay attention to the attitude of Japanese newspapers. If Japanese newspapers are always as Mr. Ishibashi commented, then there will never be a possibility of "establishing a liaison" between Chinese and Japanese newspapers. Because the people and newspapers of our country have always held an attitude of loving themselves without infringing on others, and treat the countries that treat me with equality with sincerity, equality, and peace. This has been fully demonstrated in past and present facts; if we let such people and newspapers "establish a liaison" with the kind of newspapers that Mr. Ishibashi commented on, is it possible in reality?

In short, the Chinese nation is a nation that does not invade others. The Chinese people love their own country and themselves, and also love peace and freedom. If Japan can treat China equally, without harming the integrity of China's territory and administration, without aggression, and keep its promises, then we will surely be able to treat it equally and jointly maintain peace in East Asia. If Japanese newspapers can abandon the attitude that Mr. Ishibashi commented on, and can truly work hard to improve Sino-Japanese relations based on the "principle of equality," then Chinese newspapers will naturally cooperate with it and "establish a liaison." At present, the Chinese people have fully awakened and realized that the country and the nation are at the final juncture of life and death. Unless all levels unite to resist foreign aggression, it will not be enough to seek survival. Under this situation, if Japan takes an oppressive and threatening posture to deal with the Chinese people, it will inevitably be unbearable for our 400 million compatriots, and the result will inevitably be a fundamental destruction of peace in the Far East, leading to the tragedy of mutual slaughter between the two major nations of East Asia, and even causing a world war. This may not be a blessing for China, but for Japan's misfortune, as Mr. Ishibashi said, I am afraid it "will be even worse than China's!"

The Solemn and Splendid Papal Palace 206

— Ji Min

Rome, Italy

The Vatican is one of the three major buildings in Rome and is the palace where the Roman Pope resides. It is located at the western end of Rome, occupying an area of about 450,000 square meters. In 1929, Italy and the Pope concluded a treaty in Rome and established Vatican City. In this city, the Pope has his own political sovereignty, and all the hundreds of citizens in the city are under the jurisdiction of the Pope and have nothing to do with the administration of Rome, although this place is in Rome. At the same time, the Pope has also sent ambassadors to Western European countries and South America; when any festivals arrive, many European and American countries will specially entertain his envoys.

Due to time constraints, we did not have an audience with the Pope, so we cannot talk about his demeanor and appearance here; what we want to say is the solemnity of the Vatican's architecture and all its ancient monuments and scenic spots, because although these are all manifestations of religious consciousness, they also have great cultural significance.

The so-called Vatican means the palace of the king of law, the government of the king of law. Included in Vatican City are St. Peter's Basilica, the Papal Palace, museums, libraries, chapels, gardens, etc. When we go to the Vatican in Rome, as soon as we get off the tram, what appears in front of us is an oval square surrounded by neat and beautiful corridors. Standing on the roof of the corridor are one hundred and sixty-three statues of saints, which are particularly eye-catching. As for the size of the oval square, the long diameter is 340 meters and the short diameter is 240 meters; it spreads out broadly on the ground, like a fishing net, swallowing visitors one by one. It is said that this square was designed by Bernini, a representative writer of the Italian Baroque in the 17th century. In the center of the square stands an obelisk transported from Egypt; to its left and right are two clear springs that spray white smoke into the South European sky.

On the front of the square is St. Peter's Basilica. This temple covers an area of 15,160 square meters and was completed over a long period of time from the mid-15th century to the end of the 17th century. The solemnity and greatness of its architecture can be imagined. Those who visit this temple, standing in the square, will of course first see its dome-like round roof. There is a large cross on the roof, which makes every Christian look up with reverence. It is said that this round roof was designed by Michelangelo, a great artist of the Renaissance period, in his later years. It can be said to be a noble artistic treasure. Walking into the temple and looking up at the inside of the round roof, you can immediately see the statues of Christ, St. Mary, and the ambassadors. Inside the entire temple, there are countless artistic treasures, which can be said to be an art treasure house of the Renaissance and Baroque periods. For example, Michelangelo's marble sculpture "Pieta," made in 1498, is a representative work of art of the Renaissance period; Bernini's bronze canopy (29 meters high) decorated on the high altar is also a representative of the Baroque of the 17th century, and there are many other valuable works of art that cannot be listed one by one.

Leaving St. Peter's Basilica, walking around the back from his left to the right, is the rectangular museum. As soon as you pass through the gate where this museum connects to the temple, the first thing you will see is the ancient-style guards, which will make people feel like they are leaving reality. The museum is not very simple. It includes corridors, chapels, and many buildings related to the Papal Palace. The Papal Palace here was moved from southern France by Pope Gregory XI in 1377, and later generations of popes added and renovated this palace to make it what it is today.

The walls and roofs of every house in the Vatican have been decorated by the masters of the painting world during the Renaissance. If you want to view all these paintings, it will take at least a day. Now, let us mention a few of the most valuable works of art among them.

First of all, what deserves special mention is the artistic heritage that the painting saint Raphael left us here. At the beginning of the 16th century, it was the era of Pope Julius II, the protector of art, and his court was the center of the highest culture at that time. Raphael was only twenty-nine years old at this time, and had not yet become famous. He originally lived in Florence, and only went to Rome in September 1508 at the invitation of the Pope. From this time on, he dedicated his life's energy to the frescoes of the Vatican. The most famous of the paintings he painted on the walls of Nicholas V's room are "The Fire in the Borgo," which is based on a legend from the ninth century, "The Discussion of the Holy Sacrament," which symbolizes the victory of the Catholic Church, "Parnassus," which is based on the gathering of Greek gods, and "The School of Athens," which praises the prosperity of ancient Athenian learning; in these famous paintings, we can see the cultural form of the Renaissance, where the traditional Christian thought of the Middle Ages and the reborn ancient pagan culture are in harmony.

Among the famous paintings of the painting saint Raphael, "The Discussion of the Holy Sacrament" and "The School of Athens" have particularly noble artistic value. The former's characters are divided into two types: the heavenly realm and the lower realm; in the crowd in the lower realm, you can see Dante and Savonarola, and you can also see Raphael's acquaintance, the architect Bramante. The meaning of this work goes without saying that it symbolizes the victory of Catholic theology. As for "The School of Athens," it symbolizes the victory of science; in this painting, there are many famous philosophers and scientists of ancient Greece centered on Plato and Aristotle, and you can also see Raphael's own face. Both of these paintings are the most famous works in art history, and everyone who visits the Vatican should especially appreciate them.

In addition, in the room called "Raphael Loggia," there are also scenes from the Old and New Testaments painted by Raphael; this is also a very famous and great work.

Secondly, there are many famous paintings in the Sistine Chapel, which was built by Sixtus IV in 1473. Most of these famous paintings are works from 1481-83, and they are all based on the themes of the Mosaic Tradition and Christ. Their authors are Perugino, Pinturicchio, Botticelli, and Signorelli, etc. At the same time, on the dome of this chapel, there are also paintings by Michelangelo from 1508-10. The theme of this painting is selected from the Old Testament Holy Scriptures, and around it are seven prophets and five female prophets; there are also many crowds, all of whom are naked figures with powerful muscles, they are dancing and showing different postures, showing a sentimental mood.

At the same time, on the large wall of the altar on the front of the chapel, there is a large mural painted by Michelangelo from 1534-41, which is the famous "The Last Judgment." This painting is 20 meters high and 10 meters wide, and it depicts a large group of naked figures showing a dramatic scene, and another group of naked people playing music. The greatness of its arrangement and the vividness of its expression are really rare in the history of modern painting.

The museum is divided into three parts: one is to display ancient works of art from Egypt, Greece, Etruria, Rome, etc., the second is a display room mainly for Italian paintings from the 13th to the 16th centuries, and the other is a display room for Raphael's paintings. In these display rooms, in addition to the works of art mentioned above, there are also many artistically valuable heritages, but this is not

Page 21

discussed in detail here.

In addition, in the library, there are 50,000 valuable manuscripts and many historical letters, which are also valuable items owned by the Vatican, and of course, they are also what everyone who comes here to visit pays special attention to.

Yu Yan Bamboo dispels anger, and it is not a master-apprentice relationship, and it is not forced by others. This painting is actually seen by Qing, and he likes it, so he gave it as a gift and added a small poem to read.

The clear dew flows in the morning, the empty green is clean. Combine to make autumn light cold. Thousands of acres assist Qingju. Putting paper Cha Ya. All are wind and thunder. Du Mu's army sound will enter the chant. I was kissed by the bearded Su. I also borrowed to talk about soldiers. Thousands of horses are restless. All are vertical shadows.

Mr. Ren Zhongshu of Shanyin is good at, and also paints, sings, and is not proficient in Gangfu. He died young, and the scholar-officials mourned his death. His friends and disciples specially gathered at Jingtu Temple today to mourn him, to express their sorrow. The three chapters of the right words are said to be his posthumous works. (Editor)

Humorous Sketches

An Ode to the Nose 208

— Translated by Qian Boming

Have you ever considered, dear reader, how admirable the organ of the nose is?

The nose; yes, the nose. It is the nose, this very thing, that is so useful to every animal, as Ovid (Roman poet - translator) said, lifting its face to the heavens!

Ah, it seems strange, a great act of ingratitude, that no poet has ever thought to write a lyrical poem for the nose!

Therefore, this task is left to me, but I am not a poet, I can only ask to be placed after our greatest poets and accept such an opinion.

Indeed, the nose is unfortunate.

For the eyes, so many things have been created: songs, toasts, and kaleidoscopes, paintings, landscapes, and spectacles.

For the ears: earrings, of course, go without saying, as well as the Stradivarius violin, the Erard piano, and the saxophone.

For the mouth: there is the Lenten (religious ritual of the forty days before Easter - translator) bland cooking, the nutritionist's recipe, the gourmet's culinary dictionary. They prepare all kinds of soups for it, from Russian broth to French cabbage soup; many foods for the mouth are also related to the fame of the greatest figures, from the Soubise cutlet to the Lü Xiaolu pudding: its lips are compared to coral, its teeth to pearls, and its breath to fragrance. Previously, it has eaten unfeathered peacocks and snipe with ungutted entrails; as for the future, it still has the hope of eating various roasted larks.

But what has been created for the nose? Only rose oil and snuff.

In fact, the nose is the most loyal to you. The eyes sleep, the mouth closes, the ears do not hear, but the nose is always on duty. It takes care of your sleep and contributes to your health. Feet, hands, and all other parts of the body are dull. Hands often do foolish things, feet stumble, and the body falls because of their clumsiness. When they do so, they can be carefree, but the poor nose is punished for their mistakes.

Have you not often heard it said: "So-and-so broke his nose"?

Since the beginning of time, there have been countless broken noses. But who can give a simple example to prove that a broken nose is its own fault? No one. Nevertheless, the poor nose is often scolded.

Ah, it endures all this with natural patience. Indeed, it sometimes snores rudely; but where, when have you ever heard your own nose snoring?

Now, let us forget the usefulness of the nose for a moment and pay attention to it solely from an aesthetic point of view.

The nose is like a cedar on Mount Lebanon, trampling a clump of bristles underneath; a central pillar that supports the two arches of the eyebrows. At its center dwells sharp thought; it wrinkles with a smile. The nose of the Great Conde—his greatness really came from his nose—in Lens and Rocroi, when the Spanish invaded, there their conquerors bravely wielded the staff of command, the Great Conde's nose entered before the others, and also before the Great Conde himself. Drouot's nose protruded before the crowd, his nose knew how to make twenty-four different kinds of twists, each time interesting.

No, I do not believe that the nose should be treated with ingratitude and still be forced to remain in the dark.

I propose a reason why the nose suffers under this injustice, which is that Western noses are so small.

How terrible it would be if Western noses were the only noses. But those Eastern noses, especially the noses of Georgia (a place name in old Russia - translator), are all extremely beautiful and huge noses.

Gentlemen of Paris, Vienna, and St. Petersburg, have you questioned the superiority of your own noses? In that case, my Viennese friends, go down the Danube River; you Parisians, take a boat; St. Petersburg people, take a sled; and say this simple sentence: "Go to Georgia."

However, I warn you in advance that you will be greatly humiliated. Even if you bring one of the largest noses in Europe to the gates of Tiflis (a place name near Georgia - translator), the people there will stare at you in amazement and say: "How pitiful, this gentleman dropped his nose on the road."

Ah, God - these beautiful Georgian noses! Strong noses, great noses! They come in various shapes: round, fat, long, large. They come in various colors: white, pink, deep red, violet. Some are adorned with rubies, some with pearls; I saw one adorned with turquoise.

In Georgia, King Vakhtang IV (name of an emperor in the old Russian era - translator) abolished meters and the yard system and only used the nose system. All goods must be measured by the nose. They say: "I bought seventeen noses of flannel to make pajamas, seven noses of wool to make a pair of pants, and one and a half noses of satin to make a bow tie." And in general, Georgian women find this measurement more convenient than European measurements.

Book Review

Review of "Cosmic Wind" Issue 26 209

— Senran

—Published at No. 10, Yugu Village, Yuyuan Road, this city, priced at _ corner per issue—

"Cosmic Wind," in the impression of general readers, seems to be a publication that makes humor; as soon as it is mentioned, people will think of "The Analects." However, after reading the twenty-sixth issue of "Cosmic Wind," I felt that it was not humorous, although the editors were still those famous humor masters. What is the reason for this? We don't quite understand; perhaps it is because the humor masters' senses are sharp, and they feel that in the current situation, talking about coolness is a bit "this road is blocked."

The twenty-sixth issue of "Cosmic Wind" came up with a special issue, which followed the twenty-fifth issue, with the general title of "Special Issue on Japan and the Japanese, Part II." Most of what is discussed in it is about Japanese culture and the lives of Japanese people. As for the significance of the publication of this special issue, it can be seen in these few sentences: "If someone loves Japanese civilization and thinks that everything about it is good, and tries to cover up its ugliness, or if someone hates violence and overturns everything, thinking that Japan has no culture, these are both equally wrong." These are the words of Mr. Zhou Zuoren in "Talking about Japanese Culture Books," and the publication specially excerpted them and printed them in red on the cover; its intention is undoubtedly to tell us: the publication's reason for publishing that special issue and its attitude towards the question can be expressed by Mr. Zhou's words. If the meaning of those few sentences is further extended and explained in connection with the content of this special issue, it is to arouse our attention to Japanese culture and the lives of Japanese people, to make us know its good and bad points, its strengths and weaknesses, so as to correct our own shortcomings and remedy our own weaknesses. This kind of expression is of course beyond reproach, but after reading the special issue of "Cosmic Wind," what we first felt was that some of the advantages of Japanese culture and Japanese people mentioned in the special issue are not worth praising, let alone worth learning from. For example, the article "The Life and Entertainment of Japanese Women" boasted about how Japanese women are "diligent, thrifty, gentle, and obedient," and how they have "etiquette," and even praised the "kneeling and sending off a customer by a Japanese female clerk" and the "kneeling and deeply thanking a guest for a tip by a maid," saying that this is "good service" to customers and a manifestation of understanding "etiquette." It is true that Japanese women have many advantages, and "diligence," "gentleness and obedience," and emphasis on "etiquette" are also worthy of praise, but serving men in that way, "kneeling and kowtowing" to guests in that way, seems to be too "gentle and obedient" and too much "etiquette." Women are also human beings, not slaves, so why just "kneel and kowtow" to please men or guests? Although Chinese women have not yet completely broken free from the shackles of old etiquette, they have not yet "

Continues on page five

Page 22

Page 23

Kneeling to send off" men, this point can also be said to be a place where Chinese women are not as good as Japanese women, but our female compatriots do not seem to feel ashamed because of this, and of course there is no need to learn "kneeling and kowtowing" from Japanese women. In this way, what is the significance of that special praise for Japanese women's ability to "kneel and kowtow"?

Speaking of Japanese entertainment, some of them are indeed more noble and elegant than those of China, but the Chinese entertainment industry is not completely insignificant. For example, in recent years, Chinese films (if films can be said to be a kind of entertainment) have made great progress, and some films can even be said to be better than Japanese films. However, the author of "The Life and Entertainment of Japanese Women," in addition to greatly praising Japanese films about science and military affairs, completely negated Chinese films and said that they were all worthless. He said: "Their (referring to the Japanese) films are mostly about science and military affairs, such as the manufacture and use of submarines, the combat power of tanks, and the reconnaissance and destruction of enemy situations by aircraft, which are their main themes. It is far less than our country's ability to specially manufacture such scientific educational tools into deeds that 'induce people to walk on the road of depravity.' If you don't believe me, just look at what kind of films they think are the most fashionable and popular in this time of serious national crisis. Needless to say, they are either cheesy and obscene love films or superstitious masterpieces that cheat people to death; other than that, our country's film companies do not have the resources to do it, and even if they can, they will not be able to recover their costs because they do not suit the tastes of the general public." In this way, Chinese films are all "cheesy love films" and "superstitious masterpieces that cheat people to death," and these are all produced because of the demands of the general public, so all responsibility should of course be borne by the public. I don't know if this gentleman has seen domestic films in recent years. According to what we know, films such as "Song of the Fishermen," "Goddess of Freedom," "Peach and Plum Calamity," and "The Stray Lamb" can even be said to be unsurpassed by general foreign films; and those "unplayable" dramas and films are even more suitable for the current urgent needs. However, this gentleman did not pay attention and completely negated all domestic films, which is really puzzling! As for those Japanese films that show "aircraft reconnaissance of enemy situations and destruction of enemy sides," in our view, they are consistent with their national conditions and have a great relationship with the liberation of the Chinese nation, but this gentleman did not clearly indicate that significance to arouse the attention of the people of the country and the world; he indicated only praise: this also makes us a little inexplicable!

Mr. Zhou Zuoren said in "Talking about Japanese Culture Books," after he talked about some of the advantages of Japanese culture: "What I want to mention here in passing is what is the use of talking about these cultures. To be honest, this is useless. The good aspects may not be able to save the country, and the bad aspects will not lead to selling the country. Recently, there have been some fashionable calls, such as cultural aggression or cultural traitors, but in my opinion, culture is also somewhat powerless in this relationship." Therefore, although this issue of "Cosmic Wind" introduced us to some of the cultural situation of Japan and the living conditions of the Japanese people, it did not closely link these with the current Sino-Japanese relations for discussion; it did not even mention the many ways in which Japan deals with us in terms of culture. This situation makes us even more unable to say that this special issue has no realistic and active effect.

At the same time, the Japanese culture described in this special issue is only the fragmented impressions of each author, and it has not enabled us to have an overall understanding of Japanese culture; moreover, those Japanese cultural phenomena that they talked about are only extremely superficial, and they have not been able to more deeply explore why Japan has those cultural phenomena. For example, they pointed out that Japan accepts Western and Chinese culture and forms it into its own culture. But how can Japan do this? This can of course only be explained from its social development, because a certain cultural phenomenon is produced by a certain social form; that is, a country's acceptance of another country's culture is only possible because the social forms of the two are somewhat similar, otherwise it is impossible to accept it. Take Gorky's novels and read them aloud to the uncivilized Indians in the Americas, and those people will not immediately accept the ideas in the novels and become the most progressive group of people; take a batch of American machines and transport them to Qinghai and Inner Mongolia, and they will not suddenly become the highest capitalist society and accept American culture. What is the reason for this? In a word, it is because the two do not have similar social lives, and there are no groups of people with similar lives. "Cosmic Wind" pointed out that Japan accepts Eastern and Western cultures, but did not explain its social essence and its relationship with Western Europe and Chinese society, so we can only superficially know some Japanese cultural phenomena, and we cannot have a deep understanding of it.

Naturally, some of the Japanese cultural phenomena and the strengths of some Japanese people's lives recorded in the special issue, such as Japan's progressive literature, many artistic techniques, the styles of Japanese newspapers and magazines and their attention to technology in various aspects, and the diligence and thrift of Japanese people's lives, are all things that we should learn. However, in my opinion, it is natural to learn from the strengths of the Japanese, but in the current situation, simply learning those things on the surface will not make us rich and strong. Since the Reform Movement of 1898 and the Revolution of 1911, have we not been working hard to Westernize? But as a result, on the one hand, there are naturally some good gains, but on the other hand, have not the Westernized lives of comprador businessmen and the extravagance of general Western venues been produced? Has it not made our culture increasingly manifest as a colonialized culture in many places? The reason for this is that the fundamental issue of national independence has not been thoroughly resolved, and we cannot melt other people's things and make them our own. Therefore, in the current China, to talk about accepting other people's culture, it must be discussed together with the fundamental issue of national independence in order to have positive significance. But "Cosmic Wind's" special issue failed to do this.

In addition to the special issue, there are several articles in this issue of "Cosmic Wind" that are worth reading, such as Mr. Guo Moruo's serialized "On the Way to the Northern Expedition" and Mr. Lao She's "Rickshaw Boy," although we only saw a part of them in this issue, we also felt the benefits of these two works. There are also Lao Xiang's "The Record of Taking the Exam," He Rong's "The Record of Invigilating," and short articles such as Kang De's "Saving the Country with Harmony," Li An's "Social Customs," and Fu's "Abandoning Learning to Take the Exam," which are all very good; especially those articles describing and evaluating our examination system are written truthfully and movingly. Based on these, we still have reason to say here: "Cosmic Wind" also has its advantages; compared to "The Analects," it is much more progressive. As for the shortcomings of its special issue mentioned above, that is also a criticism of some of its expressions, and it does not mean that this publication is all poisonous juice and cannot be read. On the contrary, compared to those publications that treat cheesiness as interesting and specialize in human beauty, and even those popular gentleman's publications, "Cosmic Wind" has its points that are worth recommending.

Various Industry Surveys

Poultry Trade 210

— Zhu Weiyuan

"Killing a chicken to prepare millet" has become an old saying for treating guests with respect. At the same time, Shanghai people add dishes like "white cut chicken," "roasted duck," and "soy sauce duck"; Cantonese restaurants offer "soy sauce chicken"; Nanjing people run shops selling "salted duck" and "duck gizzards"; Peking restaurants run by Shandong people offer "Peking duck"; and in Anhui restaurants, you can eat "Phoenix Wonton" (chicken and duck cooked together in one pot). These all show the close relationship between poultry and people.

New-style chicken farms in Shanghai are indeed increasing day by day, attracting much attention from society. Interviews and introductions are abundant. This article specifically introduces the situation of old-style poultry traders. From the mid-autumnal seventh lunar month to the mid-autumnal ninth lunar month is the peak season for chicken, duck, and goose trading (spring is the quietest). The total amount traded by merchants in the local north and south markets (Sixteen Pux and Dongjiadu) and Pudong, Tangqiao, and other places is worth about one million several hundred thousand yuan. In addition, there are several hundred thousand that either do not go through merchants or are handled by smaller merchants, totaling more than two million yuan. Why is autumn the busiest season? It is said that the reason why spring is the quietest is that the preserved meats stored by people in winter (such as wind-dried chicken, cured meat, sausages, etc.) have not yet been eaten. By the time the preserved meats are finished, it is already gradually getting warmer, and people do not like to eat greasy food and prefer to eat more vegetarian dishes. After summer is over, the autumn breeze brings coolness, the mind is clear, and the appetite is sure to open up. Therefore, at this time, everyone wants to eat and drink, seeking pleasure in food. Delicious chicken and duck are, of course, the objects of desire, and the cooking in restaurants at this time is even more pleasing. According to general poultry merchants, veteran gourmets, and kitchen stewards, the varieties of chicken and duck in this city are quite interesting. Now, let's describe the approximate situation of the place of origin of chickens and ducks and the traditional trade habits:

(1) Pudong Chicken: Also known as local chicken, its body shape is square, quite heavy, with sparse feathers and varied colors, mostly yellow with green and black spots. It often has feathered feet, quite like a foreign breed. It can weigh up to eight or nine pounds, hence the name "Nine-Pound Yellow." Its incubation and brooding instincts are very developed, and the meat tastes very good. If it can be improved, it can become a good meat chicken, not difficult to rival the foreign Cochin.

(2) Chongming Chicken: The body shape is similar to the local chicken, the feather color is mostly light. The feet are also [missing character], the body weight is also large, the body is quite strong, and it lays many eggs, reaching more than one hundred and fifty a year.

(3) Tongzhou Chicken: That is, the chickens produced in Nantong Prefecture and Rugao and Taixing counties. The body shape is square and slightly longer, the feather color is mostly black, more compact than Pudong chickens, the leg color is uneven, and there are slight feathers on the feet. The body weight is slightly smaller, the meat tastes good, and it lays more than one hundred eggs a year. The chicks are very easy to raise.

(4) Huaian Chicken: That is, the chickens produced in the old Huaian Prefecture, such as [missing character] Jiang, Huaicheng, and other counties. The body weight is smaller than Pudong and Chongming chickens, with blue legs and bird beaks, and is not very popular. The feather color is also not uniform. The most deaths occur after this chicken arrives in port, probably due to the hardship of traveling a long distance?

(5) Black-boned Chicken: Commonly known as woolly chicken, imported from Songjiang and various ports in Jiangbei, but not many people raise it, so there are very few people in the trade. The feather color is pure white and slightly curled, the mouth and legs are all black, very short, and the belief in protecting chicks is extremely strong. The meat quality is also good, and people in Guangdong and Fujian love to eat it the most. This chicken is generally used for appreciation, so the price is very expensive, mostly sold by pigeon and game shops.

(6) Port Duck: There are distinctions between port ducks, Yangzhou ducks, and Yangtze River ducks. Those produced in the old Tongzhou prefecture, such as Rugao and other places, are called "port"; those produced in the old Yangzhou prefecture, such as Gao, Bao, Xing, Tai, Dong, and Jiangdu counties, are called "Yangzhou"; those produced along the Yangtze River, such as Wuhu and Nanjing, are called "Yangtze River". The three types are very similar in shape, and only those experienced in this field can distinguish them. Port ducks are not very large but are easy to fatten, with yellow feet and bird beaks, mottled feathers, high tail, and legs behind the body. At first glance, you know that it is a breed good at laying eggs. Gaoyou ducks (Yangzhou) produce eggs with double yolks, which are very popular. This kind of duck is extremely easy to raise, so Gaoyou duck eggs are very famous.

(7) Goose: All areas north of the Yangtze River produce them, but those produced in the old Yangzhou prefecture are more numerous. The feathers are white, the beak is yellow, the legs are also yellow, the crown is tall, and the body weight can reach more than twenty pounds. The male's call is loud, early-maturing, easy to fatten, and the meat quality is also good, but the goslings are not easy to raise. Cantonese people love to eat goose the most, and Muslims use goose oil instead of lard and beef tallow.

The source of chickens and ducks for daily use in this city, in addition to the above-mentioned places, Danyang, Liyang and other places also produce many ducks, and many are imported into this city. As for the poultry trade, it is divided into north and south markets. The south market refers to Dongjiadu, and the north market refers to Sixteen Pux; it does not refer to South Shanghai and Zhabei. There are five large poultry shops in the south market: three chicken shops, Shen Dachang, Shen Chang, and Yishengyuan; and two duck shops, Xin Changshun and Nan Defeng; all located in the Dongjiadu area of ​​Pubin. There are eight in the north market: Defeng, Wanfeng, Puyi, Hemei, Xieji, all located on Wai Ma Road; Taihefeng, Hongda, and Yutai, all located in Lao Taiping Lane. In addition, there are three shops on Wai Ma Road, Hengda, Gongji, and Hengtai, but they specialize in ducks and game, such as wild ducks, old wild ducks, and egrets. The other chicken and duck shops, such as Chen Yongfeng and Defeng in Lao Taiping Street, Yu Longji in Zengxiang Street, Zhao Mingji in Jiyong Street, and Chen Tongxing in Huiguan Street, are not merchants, but buy and resell from merchants to vendors, so they are not included in the public office. The equipment of each shop is to place chicken and duck cages in front of the store. The scales used are all issued by the public office. Merchants provide food and lodging to guests, so bedding must be prepared, but the temporary feed for chickens and ducks is the responsibility of the vendors. Speaking of transportation, most are transported by boat to Sixteen Pux and landed. Customers are free to submit to a merchant. After designation, the shop assistants will transport the chickens and ducks to the shop and are not allowed to solicit on the way. As for vendors, they use small carts to load cages and transport them to Zhabei, Hongkou, Qiujiang Road, Miller Road, and other places. In the south market, they are in the Xuejia Bang and Li Ma Road areas; in the Public Concession, they are in Tie Fangzi and Xiaocai Chang; in the French Concession, they are in Caishi Road and other places. The poultry trade has the organization of the Shanghai Juyuantang Poultry Industry Public Office, its address is in Lao Taiping Street. The public office has 20 public rules set in the year of Jiazi of the Republic of China, and there are also rules for the industry to rectify the sale of chickens, ducks, and geese, which are serious. As for the tax situation, it only started to be recognized at the end of the Qing Guangxu period, with a total amount of 1,300 silver yuan; by the 14th year of the Republic of China, it gradually increased to 4,920 yuan; after the 15th year of the Republic of China, it increased to 8,000 yuan. Those who enter the chicken and duck public office must have a capital of at least 30,000 yuan, because too little capital may lead to the risk of bankruptcy, which will affect the public office. Those who opened after the eighth year of the Republic of China must pay a public office fund of 500 yuan, because after the merchants go bankrupt, the public office must be responsible for maintaining the aftermath.

In the 18th year of the Republic of China, the poultry merchants Qiao Zhongxian and others submitted a request to the Social Bureau for permission to establish a trade association. Its members included 19 companies such as Puyi and Hemei, but there were more than one hundred dozens of companies engaged in transporting and selling chickens and ducks. The eggs of chickens and ducks are especially essential daily foods. It is estimated that there are more than 50 egg shops in this city, such as Maochang, Lu Boji, Xiji, Xiehe, Zhu Shenchang, and Xu Xinji, and there is also a trade association, which has close contact with the poultry trade, because "chickens are inseparable from eggs, and eggs are inseparable from chickens."

In the new-style chicken farms that improve chicken breeds, no effort is spared to improve eggs, but because the selling price is slightly higher, it is not popular after all, so the business of the egg shops is more prosperous. As for the factories in this city that process egg products and manufacture dry egg white and egg yolk powder, there are more than 30 in total, and 20 have joined the trade association. Because these egg factories are responsible for supplying the raw materials for the daily necessities of cakes, biscuits, egg rolls, and other snack foods. Its factory names include more than 20 companies such as Qian Yuan, Huaxing, Fengyu, Hexing, Huachang, Dingji, Qingcheng, Hongchang, Hongxin, Qingfeng, Dingsheng, Tongxin, Hong Yuchang, Yuansheng, Hongsheng, Han Xingxiang, Dingfeng, Zengxin, Xin Chang, and Songyuan.

Literary Works

Going Back to My Hometown (9) 211

— David

"No, there's no money in the box at all!" I answered firmly, despising them in my heart.

"Really nothing?"

"Really nothing!" I got a little angry.

"Open it and take a look!"

My face turned red, and I opened the box. The old image was impatient.

The policeman came over, flipped through it casually, and then dodged away.

The police officer questioned us: where we came from and the purpose of coming to "Xinjing". He asked very easily, not as strict as before.

We all felt relieved and answered him: we came from Fengtian and wanted to seek refuge at the "Datong College" in "Xinjing".

They all slowly backed out.

"God! Why did they want to joke with us!" The old image was overjoyed.

"Calm down! Outside..." I stopped the old image.

The accountant came over, and I asked him:

"What's the matter? Why are you checking the shop?"

"Don't you know, there was a robbery on Sanma Road at eight o'clock tonight." His small round eyes turned tightly after he finished speaking, and he walked away hurriedly.

I came in and told them the news, and everyone smiled at each other.

Yes: sensuality, gambling, tobacco and alcohol, theft, robbery, bullying, all of this is what we saw and heard during our more than 30 hours stay in the political center of "Kandao".

At twelve o'clock at night, we squeezed into the old train on the Harbin-Changchun Railway again.

This solid old carriage still hasn't changed its original shape, it's like seeing an old friend.

There were no lights in the car, and we were all groping in the darkness, groping.

We barely squeezed into a few seats, and the people sitting on both sides were all famine victims from Shandong.

A six- or seven-year-old child was so tired that he had nowhere to sleep, so his mother pushed him down on the floor of the car. The child didn't care about the dirt and saliva and fell asleep sweetly.

A sharp light shot from the left; behind the light, leading a yellow-clothed "police officer", slowly walked to the sleeping child.

"Sleeping is not allowed!..." He asked the child, who was fast asleep, viciously, and then kicked him with his leather shoe.

The child didn't move, and didn't breathe anymore.

He retracted the light from the electric torch and walked forward.

The mother's miserable cry, combined with the rolling sound of the wheels, shook the hearts of everyone in the car. We all quietly dodged away, unable to bear to hear the wailing of this weak person!

The stars twinkled sadly in the sky, as if crying for this little soul.

The dark and vast earth was covered with countless shadows; we, this group of weak people, all threw ourselves into its dark embrace.

The turbid morning mist and the coal smoke spewed out by the train's engine were intertwined, [missing character] [missing character] a [missing character], covering the ground

In the east, behind this layer of turbid mist, a pale red circle appeared.

The vegetable vendor, carrying a load on his shoulder, the cold made him turn with tears in his eyes; he stood impatiently outside the fence, waiting to cross the railway.

A group of stray dogs surrounded the back of the "killing cattle house", looking for discarded cattle bones.

I concentrated my attention and stretched my head out of the car window, looking for the house I lived in ten years ago.

The old image woke up from a nap and pushed me, saying, "Where are we? Why didn't you call us!"

"We're at Shanghao!"

They all woke up with a start, vying to look out the window.

Ah! I was so happy that tears came out. I wanted to jump out of the car window and kiss the little Latin-style house that I had been away from for ten years.

Its red-tiled roof stood there brightly and proudly, covered with a layer of dew. The small fence surrounding it, the few trees in front of the courtyard gate, and the white iron can skins [missing character] in the garbage pile on the left side of the house were all the same as when I lived here ten years ago, as if nothing had changed. But what about my gentle Russian hostess and her innocent and lovely Little Lina? In the courtyard surrounded by the fence, I vaguely saw some clothes that looked like Japanese clothes being dried. The big sleeves were blown by the wind, fluttering back and forth.

All of this, which was both intimate and unfamiliar, flashed quickly past my eyes.

The car stopped at the final destination—Harbin Qinjiagang Station.

The bustling crowd on the platform was still as crowded as it was ten years ago, but this Parisian girl from four years ago seemed to have married "×Jing", and the situation was a little different from before. The internal form of the station has completely changed, and the road names on all the road signs have been replaced with certain texts, which made us seem to understand but not understand; after bumping around for a long time, we finally rushed out of this chaotic intake and output port.

The car carrying the five of us ran along the station to Xugong Road.

Beside the road, the palace-style Third Middle School, like a fallen aristocratic son, was barely supporting itself there; the glaze on the red and green glazed tiles on the top had fallen off; the surrounding area was surrounded by layers of iron barbed wire, two bright bayonets were standing in front of the door, and a natural wooden sign was hung on the wall, with [missing character] [missing character] a few [missing character] words, like "Da××× Radio Class".

The car gasped and carried us across the intersection of Xugong Road again. Next to it, the library, which was under construction when I left Harbin, has now been completed; however, this building has not been used as a library, but has been changed to the "Harbin Provincial Police Department." (To be continued)

Home
